Opening of the Electrical Industry Inspection Conference

(Nanjing) To promote the national electrical industry, the Construction Commission convened the Electrical Industry Inspection Conference of various provinces and cities, which opened at 9:00 AM on the 6th. Representatives from the Construction Departments of Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Shandong, Shanxi, Anhui, Jiangxi, Hebei, Henan, Hunan, Shandong, and other provinces, as well as representatives from the Shanghai and Beiping Municipal Governments and the Construction Commission, totaling more than 30 people, attended. Yun Zhen presided over the meeting and delivered an opening speech. Secretary Liu Shixin delivered a speech on behalf of Zhang Renjie, titled "The Policy of This Commission for the Development of the National Electrical Industry and Expectations for the Responsible Authorities of Various Provinces and Cities." The speech stated that although China's electrical industry has gradually made progress, foreign-funded power plants still account for 88%. Now, domestic power plants find it difficult to compete. The work of this commission in charge of the electrical industry that can be reported to the people of the country includes: (1) Establishing standard frequencies and voltages and making every effort to promote them in order to establish a permanent grand plan; (2) Formulating various technical regulations; (3) Communicating the relationship between the financial sector and the electrical industry; (4) Publishing accurate investigation statistics; (5) Reorganizing state-owned power plants to set an example; (6) Cooperating with local governments; (7) Making every effort to crack down on electricity theft and spreading knowledge of electricity use; (8) Improving the treatment of technical personnel; (9) This commission will serve as a consultant to various power plants at any time; (10) Improving legal clauses. In total, there are 498 domestic power plants, of which 471 are privately operated, so it is imperative to support private operations. The way to rescue them lies in self-help. The government and the party should encourage and motivate them. This commission sincerely hopes that the responsible authorities of various provinces and cities will conduct inspections of private power plants and provide practical guidance. The central and local governments must be connected as one, so that administrative orders can be implemented without conflict. Subsequently, representatives from various provinces and cities gave reports. Discussion sessions continued in the afternoon. The conference agenda will last for three days. In addition to the discussion sessions, participants will also visit various factories in the capital. The conference will close on the 8th. (Central News Agency dispatch, 6th)

Huang Fu Returns to Beiping; Japanese Representatives Arrive in Succession to Discuss Everything; North China Diplomatic Disputes Will Seek Resolution; Huang Advocates Revitalizing Morale and Working Hard to Move Forward

— Correspondent

Beiping Special Dispatch: Huang Fu, who is responsible for the political and diplomatic affairs of North China, previously went south after receiving a telegram to discuss strategies for dealing with the current situation. Now, a considerable result has been achieved, and he has returned to the north to preside over the affairs. In the future, the political and diplomatic affairs of North China will be handled by Huang, and Sino-Japanese diplomatic relations will evolve under the theme of amity and peace. It is learned that Huang arrived in Beiping yesterday (the 4th) at 1:05 PM. Kita Seiichi, a representative of the Kwantung Army, arrived with him. Japanese Ambassador Arima and Kwantung Army Chief of Staff Okamura will also arrive in Beiping within the next two or three days to discuss various issues between China and Japan in North China with Huang Fu in detail. It is reported that after Huang's return to the north, his first priority is to seek the permanent stability of North China and gradually promote its prosperity. The second priority is to quickly resolve all current disputes. There are approximately several aspects to the current disputes: (1) After the war zone was taken over, the security forces were weak, and bandits took the opportunity to rise up, wreaking havoc at will, and threatening to spread like wildfire. In order to stabilize the local area and eliminate bandits, our side sent representatives to consult with the Japanese side to send troops to the front line to clear the countryside. After many days of negotiations, no results were obtained. As a last resort, the security forces permitted in the ceasefire agreement were quickly organized and sent to deal with the emergency. Unexpectedly, when the security forces departed from Luanzhou, they were blocked by the Japanese army on the way and forced to return. The reasons given by the Japanese side were: firstly, that our security forces had long since entered the war zone, and that those dispatched this time were additional; and secondly, that the security forces dispatched this time were reorganized from the army, which violated the agreement. In fact, our security forces, due to incomplete training and the hasty takeover last time, temporarily dispatched a portion to maintain order, and the rest were planned to be dispatched successively after training was completed. The Japanese side's claims were purely a misunderstanding. In recent days, representatives have been sent to Yuguan to negotiate with Kita, the representative of the Japanese army, and Suzuki, the brigade commander, and gradually obtained understanding. Yesterday, Kita arrived in Beiping. Today (the 5th), Huang Fu and He Yingqin hosted a banquet in Jurentang to entertain them. After the banquet, Huang, He, Kita, and Shibata, the military attache of the Japanese embassy, discussed this matter and reached a solution. The security forces will be able to go to eastern Luanzhou within a few days to engage in bandit suppression. (2) The takeover of various passes along the Great Wall has been under negotiation for a long time, but has not yet been resolved. This matter is quite complicated. There are about sixty or more passes, large and small, along the Great Wall. Except for the five major passes of Xifengkou, Gubeikou, Yuguan, Jiumenkou, and Lengkou, the remaining small passes are not currently garrisoned by the Japanese army, and the takeover is relatively easy. However, the takeover of these five major passes is quite difficult, especially Yuguan, which is an important gateway for travel between the three northeastern provinces and the interior. The puppet state has established various institutions there, and even the establishment of a customs office is proving to be extremely difficult. Since Dalian is a free trade port, in the current situation, if our side does not establish a customs office in Yuguan to collect taxes, goods from all countries can enter the interior through Dalian. In this way, not only will North China be greatly affected, but the foreign trade of the entire country will also be hit. As a result, the national tax revenue will also be sharply reduced. However, if a customs office is established in Yuguan, it seems to tacitly acknowledge that this is the boundary, and there is a tendency to tolerate the existence of the puppet organization. This is just one example; there are many other similar problems. Therefore, the takeover of various passes along the Great Wall cannot be done without considerable research and negotiation. (3) Since the troops of Fang Zhenwu and Ji Hongchang entered the war zone, the Japanese side has again used the pretext of military force to drive them out, and they have entered Huairou and other places. At the same time, the troops of Fang and Ji are actively advancing south on the border of the war zone. A solution to this complex situation needs to be found urgently. According to Huang, after returning to Beiping, he is discussing solutions with various parties.

Huang returned to Beiping yesterday afternoon at 1:00 PM. At 5:00 PM, he met with reporters at Fengzeyuan and issued the following statement: [I (Huang referred to himself) went south in early July and am only now returning north, which has been two months. During these two months, I am ashamed to have accomplished nothing. What I can report is approximately three points: (1) After going south, I reported the situation in North China to the central government and discussed various issues related to the aftermath. The central government has a deep understanding and appreciation of the environment in North China and the various complex situations. (2) The most difficult problem currently facing North China is finance. After consultation with the central government, a considerable solution has been found. It has been decided that the military expenses of North China will be restored to the original budget of 4.5 million yuan, which will be maintained by the central government. The military expenses of North China were originally 4.5 million yuan before the war, and were later increased to 5.7 million yuan due to military reasons. After the war, great efforts were made to reduce them, reducing them to 5 million yuan. Since the central government decided to restore the original budget, the Beiping Military Branch has repeatedly held meetings to reduce expenses, and has now reached a considerable level, which is not much different from what the central government intended. Minister Song believes that if the financial situation in North China remains in its current chaotic state, there is no solution. He advocates that it should be completely under the central government, and find ways to reorganize it, so that it can be saved. I have no preconceived notions about this. It has now been decided that the financial affairs of North China will be completely under the central government, which should be more manageable in the future. (3) Relief for war victims is a major problem in North China. The central government has changed its plans for relief in the war zone several times. The initial plan was to allocate 20 million yuan for relief, but due to various reasons, it was changed to 5 million yuan, of which 1 million yuan was in cash to handle emergency relief, and 4 million yuan was in public bonds to relieve rural areas. The cash has already been remitted before I went south. The public bonds must wait until the regulations are passed before they can be issued. These regulations have long been reported to the central government, but have not yet been passed by the Legislative Yuan. I do not know the reason. Only after going south did I learn that there were some disputes over the public bond fund. It has now been completely resolved. It should be passed this week or next week, and the issuance date is not far away. The above three points are the most important issues that I can report. In addition, I have also participated in the discussion of the overall national problem because it is related to North China, and generally have considerable results. As for personal feelings, I have talked about them when passing through Nanjing, Jinan, and Tianjin. Recalling the day I first arrived in Beiping on May 17th, enemy planes soared over Beiping, and the sound of enemy cannons shook the suburbs. The tension was so great that there was no room for delay. In order to comfort the people of the country, I put forward the slogan of stabilizing people's hearts. Although the situation is now more relaxed, it has not yet reached a stable level. The word "stability" should be changed to "revitalization." In the current difficult environment, there is no other way but to revitalize people's hearts and work hard to move forward. There was a slight misunderstanding between China and Japan regarding the suppression of bandits in eastern Luanzhou. Now, after negotiation, there is complete understanding. The security forces will be able to go there soon to eliminate bandits, which can be expected. The takeover of various passes along the Great Wall is no longer a problem for the small passes. The five major passes are complicated and still require a considerable period of negotiation and research to be resolved.] (October 5th)

Fang Zhenwu and Ji Hongchang Invade Northern Beiping; Fierce Fighting in the Gaoliying Area; People from Northern Beiping Flee to Beiping for Refuge; Japanese Troops Increasingly Active in the War Zone

Beiping Special Dispatch: The troops of Fang Zhenwu and Ji Hongchang have repeatedly attacked Changping since the 1st of this month, plotting to cut off the Ping-Sui Railway. On the 3rd, they retreated from the vicinity of Qincheng and Daxiaohongmen in the northeast of Changping to Tangshan Gaoliying. One route attacked Datangshan from Xingshou Qincheng, and the other route passed through Mayu, Yulin Garden, Xiangtun, and other places, and occupied the vicinity of Gaoliying. The troops in Tangshan suddenly occupied Datangshan yesterday (the 4th). This morning (the 5th), a detachment advanced from Pingzhuang towards Xiaotangshan. A certain regiment stationed in Xiaotangshan gathered its forces in Langou, Tangtou Village, Suanzaoling, and other places, and tried its best to defend. At 7:00 AM this morning, Fang Ji's cavalry was also discovered in Mafang, four or five li south of Xiaotangshan. It clashed with the stationed troops. After an hour of contact, Fang Ji's troops retreated slightly. Then, more than 1,000 infantrymen counterattacked, and fierce fighting broke out again. In the afternoon, the fighting subsided somewhat, and the two sides were in a stalemate, with occasional clashes. Yesterday, Fang Ji's troops were also discovered in Dadongliu and Xiaodongliu, west of Gaoliying. The stationed troops were alerted and immediately went to block them. After a day of fierce fighting, Fang Ji's troops finally retreated to Gaoliying, but then used surprise troops to approach Lishui Bridge, south of Gaoliying. Due to strategic reasons, the stationed troops temporarily abandoned Gaoliying and returned to attack. At the same time, the authorities here believed that Lishui Bridge was only more than 30 li away from Beiping, which was of great importance, and sent a large army to reinforce it. Only then were Fang Ji's troops repelled. Today, fierce fighting is still taking place in the vicinity of Gaoliying and Lishui Bridge. The national army is densely deployed north of Lishui Bridge, in Taipingzhuang, Lishuyuan, and in the vicinity of Xiaotangshan, Mafang, and Baxianzhuang, forming a large encirclement. There should be developments within a few days. Wan Fulin personally went to the front line yesterday to make arrangements because the military situation at the front was tight, ordering the divisions of Zhou Fucheng and Zhu Hongxun to coordinate the defense line. The Pingbei Avenue has been cut off again in recent days. The Tangshan telephone line has also been experiencing problems since yesterday. People fleeing to Beiping for refuge are constantly arriving, and the situation is very tragic. The Japanese army has used the pretext of driving out Fang Ji and entered the war zone. Not only have they not withdrawn in recent days, but they have also added more than 700 troops to Miyun, Huairou, and other places. The Fourth Brigade has established its headquarters in a certain salt shop in Miyun City, and Brigade Commander Saeda is stationed there. After the fighting broke out in Gaoliying yesterday, the Fifth Regiment of the Japanese army stationed in Huairou sent more than 50 Japanese soldiers by military vehicle to Xishuiquan Village, about five li north of Gaoliying, at 10:00 AM this morning. At 1:00 PM in the afternoon, more than 100 more arrived, claiming to prevent Fang Ji's troops from retreating into the war zone. Japanese planes have been constantly scouting and dropping bombs in recent days. This morning, a Japanese plane flew to the Gaoliying area and dropped three bombs west of Gaoliying. (October 5th, Correspondent)

Zhejiang Province's Transportation is Becoming Increasingly Developed; 1,330 Kilometers of Highways Have Been Completed; The Hangzhou-Jiangshan Railway Can Be Completed by the End of the Year; 8,165 Kilometers of Long-Distance Telephone Lines

It is well known that transportation is related to culture, economy, and military affairs. In recent years, the political situation in Zhejiang Province has been relatively stable, and the authorities have spared no effort in building highways, railways, and telephone lines. Due to unrest in neighboring provinces and bandit alarms on the border, the development of transportation is particularly urgent. It is estimated that the province needs 2,000 kilometers of highways, and 2,330.55 kilometers have been completed. The Hangzhou-Jiangshan Railway is related to the communication between the two Zhejiangs. The Jiangshan-Lanxi section was opened to traffic in the 20th year of the Republic, and the Jinhua-Yushan section is under active construction. The Jinhua-Tangxi section was opened to traffic on September 11th this year, and the entire line can be completed by the end of the year. The entire line will be opened to traffic on New Year's Day next year. Telephone lines are related to the transmission of news, and their function is no less than that of highways and railways. Currently, 8,165 li of telephone lines have been built in the province, and wireless telephones have also made considerable progress. The reporter will now describe the general situation of transportation in Zhejiang Province in detail below:

Progress of Highways

The construction of highways in Zhejiang Province began in the 16th year of the Republic. The Hangzhou-Changxing section of the Beijing-Hangzhou Road, the Hangzhou-Zhapu section of the Shanghai-Hangzhou Road, the Hangzhou-Huizhou Road (Hangzhou-Yuhang section and Lin'an-Changhua section), and the Hangzhou-Shaoxing-Yinzhou-Fenghua lines were all completed before the 19th year of the Republic, totaling 813.27 kilometers. Starting from the 19th year of the Republic, construction continued. In the 20th year of the Republic, due to the shortage of provincial treasury funds, austerity measures were implemented, which affected the construction. Therefore, the completion of various roads was mostly in the 21st and 22nd years of the Republic. A total of 517.28 kilometers of highways were completed in the three years, for a total of 1,330.55 kilometers. 975.88 kilometers are under construction, and 573.40 kilometers are under survey. If funds are available in the future, it will not be difficult to complete them as scheduled.

Completed Roads

The highways completed before the 19th year of the Republic include: the Beijing-Hangzhou Road (Hangzhou to Fuziling) 129.73 li, the Shanghai-Hangzhou Road (Hangzhou to Jinsinian Bridge) 154.35 li (the Zhapu-Jinshan section of 23.213 li was completed in the 21st year of the Republic), the Hangzhou-Shaoxing Road (Gongchen Bridge to Sanlangmiao, and Jiangbian to Shaoxing) 61.58 li, the Yinzhou-Fenghua Road (Yinzhou to Fenghua and Jiangkou to Rushanting) 49.25 li, the Hangzhou-Fuyang Road (Hangzhou to Fuyang) 53.62 li, the Hangzhou-Huizhou Road (Hangzhou-Yuhang section) 32.55 li, the Hangzhou-Huizhou Road (Lin'an-Changhua section) 40.00 li, the Shengzhou-Xinchang Road (Shengzhou to Xinchang) 14.89 li, the Quzhou-Guangfeng Road (Quzhou to Guangfeng, jointly operated by the province and merchants) 65.73 li, the Shengzhou-Changle Town Road (Shengzhou to Changle Town, the following roads are all jointly operated by merchants) 25.70 li, the Pingyao-Huzhou-Shuangxi Road (Pingyao to Shuangxi) 24.77 li, the Hangzhou-Huizhou Road (Yuhang-Lin'an section) 45.66 li, the Shaoxing-Cao'e Road (Shaoxing to Hao Ba) 36.69 li, the Shengzhou-Shanshu Tan Road (Shengzhou to Shanshu Tan) 7.00 li, the Changshan-Yushan Road (Changshan to Yushan) 21.40 li, the Yuhang-Wukang Road (Yuhang to Wukang Peng Gong Ling) 21.80 li, and the Hangzhou-Tangqi Road (Hangzhou to Tangqi) 51.68 li. The road built in the 20th year of the Republic is the Quzhou-Changshan Road (Quzhou to Changshan) 42.00 li. The roads built in the 21st year of the Republic include: the Cangzhou-Zhangshu Tan Road (Dazhou to Zhangshu Tan) 14.00 li, the Dutan-Huangjia Shan Road (Dutan to Huangjia Shan) 14.75 li, the Pujiang-Zhengjia Wu Road (Pujiang to Zhengjia Wu) 24.70 li, the Yutou-Xiakou Road (Yutou to Xiakou) 20.47 li (the above four roads are all jointly operated by merchants), the Huangyan-Leqing Road (Luqiao to Haimen section) 15.99 li, the Quzhou-Lanxi Road (Quzhou to Lanxi) 70.65 li, the Hangzhou-Huizhou Road (Changhua to Yuling Pass section) 43.00 li, and the Shanghai-Hangzhou Road (Zhapu-Pinghu branch line) 13.41 li. The roads built in the 22nd year of the Republic include: the Changxing-Si'an Road (Changxing to Si'an boundary marker) 38.02 li, the Jiaxing-Wangjiangjing Road (Jiaxing to Wangjiangjing) 15.00 li, the Yongkang-Jinyun Road (Yongkang to Jinyun) 34.00 li, the Jinhua-Wuyi-Yongkang Road (Jinhua to Yongkang and Wuyi) 62.30 li (the Jinhua-Yongkang section of 48.00 li was completed in the 22nd year of the Republic), and the Ningbo-Zhenhai-Cixi Road (Ningbo to Guanhaiwei and Xiepu to Zhenhai) 60.86 li (the trunk line of 44.18 li was completed in the 22nd year of the Republic), and the Huangyan-Leqing Road (Huangyan to Zeguo section) 25.00 li. The above totals 1,330.55 kilometers of completed highways.

Roads Under Construction

The highways under construction include: the Hangzhou-Jianqiao Road (Banshan to Jianqiao) 8.58 li, the Jinyun-Lishui Road (Jinyun to Lishui) 41.00 li, the Jiangshan-Kaihua Road (Changshan to Tongcun section) 37.00 li, the Jiangshan-Kaihua Road (Tongcun to Haoling section) 23.90 li, the Jiangshan-Kaihua Road (Xiakou to Fengling section) 35.00 li, the Cao'e-Shengzhou Road (Hao Ba to Shanshu Tan) 39.40 li, the Yiwu-Chang Le Town Road (Yiwu via Dongyang to Changle Town in Shengzhou) 71.00 li, the Hangzhou-Huizhou Road (Yuling Pass to Xia Keng section) 30.00 li, the Suichang-Kaihua Road (Huafu to Kaihua section) 23.00 li, the Fuyang-Xindeng Road (Fuyang to Xindeng Xiajiangkou) 39.00 li, the Tonglu-Jiande Road (Tonglu Shangjiang to Jiande Shili Ting) 51.00 li, the Tunxi-Jiande-Shouchang Road (Jiande to the Anhui border and Luotongbu to Shouchang) 128.00 li, the Chunan-Suian Road (Chunan to Suian) 70.00 li, the Fenghua-Xinchang Road (Rushanting to Xinchang) 57.20 li, the Lishui-Qingtian Road (Lishui to Qingtian) 72.00 li, the Pinghu-Jiaxing Road (Pinghu to Jiaxing) 28.00 li, the Ningbo-Chuanshan Road (Ningbo to Chaiqiao Xiaomen, from Chaiqiao to Chuanshan) 42.00 li, the Ningbo-Hengshan Road (Ningbo via Hanlin to Hengshanbu) 40.00 li, the Cixi-Longshan Road (Cixi via Wenxi Hetoushi to Longshan) 21.00 li, the Yuyao-Zhoushang Road (Yuyao to Zhoushang Zhen and Zhengxiang to Hushang) 28.00 li, the Lanxi-Shouchang Road (Lanxi to Shouchang) 34.80 li, and the Lishui-Yunhe Road (Lishui to Yunhe) 56.00 li, totaling 975.88 kilometers.

Roads Under Survey

The highways currently under survey include: the Yuhang-Anji Road (Yuhang Huanghu via Xiaofeng to Anji) 56.00 li, the Longyou-Songyang Road (Longyou via Suichang to Songyang) 150.00 li, the Yongjia-Ruian Road (Yongjia via Ruian to the Fujian border) 115.00 li, the Qingtian-Yongjia Road (Qingtian to Yongjia) 52.00 li, the Xinchang-Tiantai Road (Xinchang via Tiantai to Jindi) 108.40 li, the Fenghua-Ninghai Road (Fenghua to Ninghai) 44.00 li, the Xiangshan-Xitan Road (Xiangshan to Xitan) 18.00 li, and the Guanhaiwei-Zhouxiang Road (Guanhaiwei to Zhouxiang in Yuyao) 30.00 li, totaling 573.40 kilometers.

Hangzhou-Jiangshan Railway Project

The Hangzhou-Jiangshan Railway began construction in the 19th year of the Republic. The Jiangbian-Lanxi section was opened to traffic in March of the 21st year of the Republic. The Jinhua-Yushan section can be completed by the end of the year.

General Situation of the Jiangbian-Lanxi Section

The entire section is 200 kilometers long. From the date of the first survey of the Jiangzuo line in the 17th year of the Republic to the date of the completion of the entire project in May of the 22nd year of the Republic, it cost a total of 6,623,903.29 yuan. In June of the 20th year of the Republic, traffic was opened from Jiangbian to Jianshan. In July, traffic was opened to Zhuji. In December, traffic was opened to Yiwu. By February of the 21st year of the Republic, traffic was opened to Jinhua. In March, traffic was opened to Lanxi. There are a total of 21 stations. All station buildings, platforms, fences, and temporary water supply equipment along the line were completed in the 20th year of the Republic. A machine factory was also established in Xixing. There are now nine locomotives, thirty passenger cars, and eighty freight cars, which are sufficient for current use. Initially, passenger cars traveled back and forth daily, with one mixed train running each way. Subsequently, one express train and one local train were added each way daily. After traffic was opened to Lanxi, two express trains and two local trains ran each way daily. In terms of business, when traffic was opened to Jianshan in the 20th year of the Republic, monthly passenger and freight revenue was approximately 15,000 yuan. When traffic was opened to Yiwu, monthly revenue increased to more than 28,000 yuan. After traffic was opened to Jinhua and Lanxi, monthly revenue increased from 54,000 yuan to 100,000 yuan. Passenger traffic was even busier at the end of the year, reaching 130,000 to 140,000 yuan per month. In October of the 21st year of the Republic, through transport with the Shanghai-Hangzhou Railway was implemented, making travel more convenient.

The Jin-Yu Section Will Soon Be Completed

The Jin-Yu section, from Jinhua to Yushan Bingxi, is 164 kilometers long and requires approximately 6 million yuan. Besides the authorities raising 1 million yuan in cash and borrowing 200,000 pounds from the Boxer Indemnity fund to purchase materials (approximately 3.5 million yuan in national currency), another 2.5 million yuan was borrowed from a banking consortium of four banks including the Bank of China in Hangzhou. In the winter of the 21st year [of the Republic], the entire section was re-surveyed. The roadbed officially commenced construction on November 21 of the same year. The roadbed width is 4.0 meters, the track gauge is 1.435 meters, and it is a single track. The earth and stone volume of the roadbed is 3,182,000 cubic meters, divided into eight sections, contracted by the Far East Consortium and the China Industrial Development Company. Major bridges include the Jinhua River, Qingyang, Houda Creek, Xinban Creek, Zhu Creek, Mabaoxia Mountain Creek, Lingshan Port, Shangshan Creek, Dongji River, Jiangshan River, and Dukou Bridges, totaling 1605 meters. Minor bridge construction is 382 meters, culverts are 355, telephone and telegraph lines are 164 kilometers, and tracks are 174 kilometers. The entire section will have fourteen stations. The first phase will add six locomotives, 24 passenger cars, and 40 freight cars. Most bridges are of a permanent nature. Station buildings, water supply, and other facilities are temporary. All projects are scheduled to be completed by the end of the 22nd year [of the Republic]. The section from Jinhua to Tangxi was opened to traffic on September 11. Construction between Tangxi and Longyou is actively underway, and the entire line is expected to be open to traffic by the end of the year.

Installation of Telephone Lines

The long-distance telephone service in Zhejiang Province was planned and prepared in the 17th year [of the Republic]. The Hangzhou City telephone service was also taken back and managed by the province in the winter of the 18th year [of the Republic], planning the establishment of automatic telephones. The effectiveness of wireless telephones throughout the province is especially great and is also described here.

Long-Distance Telephones

Up to the 18th year [of the Republic], the main lines of Hangzhou-Fengqiao, Fengqiao-Shanghai, Hangzhou-Changxing, Hangzhou-Changshan, Hangzhou-Pinghu, and Hangzhou-Qingyuan, totaling more than 2,750 li, have been completed. After the 19th year [of the Republic], there was even greater progress. The main long-distance lines were either completed or had long-distance lines added, and rural branch lines were installed. In the 19th year [of the Republic], more than 1,736 li of telephone lines were completed, in the 20th year [of the Republic], 1,517 li were completed, and in the 21st year [of the Republic], the provincial-county cooperation method was adopted, and progress was smoother. A total of 2,045 li of telephone lines were completed, including 345.5 li of vehicle telephone lines built along with highways, and 210.5 li of branch lines under construction, with 1,489 li of actual lines built. In three years, a total of 4,742 li of lines were built, and together with the previous two years, a total of 8,165 li of lines were built. A total of 58 counties throughout the province have telephone service. There are currently seven branch bureaus (Jiaxing, Wuxing, Ningbo, Lanxi, Linhai, Shuijia, and Lishui), nineteen first-class branch bureaus, twenty-four second-class branch bureaus, and over one hundred acting offices.

Automatic Telephones

The original telephone system in Hangzhou City had outdated equipment, chaotic wiring, and was limited by the capacity of the original switchboard, failing to meet the needs of the city. After being taken back and managed by the province in the winter of the 18th year [of the Republic], the planning for automatic telephones began immediately. A rotary automatic exchange with 3,000 lines was selected. In June of the 20th year [of the Republic], the city's main exchange building was completed, and in November, the Gongchen Bridge sub-exchange building was completed. Machines were installed, underground cables were completed, and users' telephones were modified. In April of the 21st year [of the Republic], the entire project was completed and telephone service began.

Wireless Telephones

In the spring of the 17th year [of the Republic], preparations began for a broadcasting radio station. At that time, the power of the transmitter was only 250 watts. Afterwards, it increased annually, reaching 1,000 watts in the winter of the 20th year [of the Republic]. All 75 counties in the province are equipped with radios. In the summer of the 19th year [of the Republic], to strengthen defense, a telegraph station was added to the radio station. Branch stations were established in the four remote counties of Pingyang, Taishun, Qingyuan, and Longquan. Last year, branch stations were also established in Shipu, Yongjia, and Zhenhai. In addition to communicating with the branch stations, the main station also communicates with radio stations in Beijing, Shanghai, Fuzhou, Hekouzhen, Zhenjiang, Luoyang, Beiping, and Guangzhou at fixed times. Recently, a cooperative method of wired and wireless electricity has been established, using Longquan as the center, which has a great effect. In total, the 32 counties in the province far from the province and without power plants use Model 18 machines, the 40 counties near the province or with power plants use Model 16 machines, 2 counties use Milo machines, and 1 county uses an AC motor.

Kunshan: Change of the County Public Security Bureau Chief

Since Qin Jieren, the chief of the Kunshan County Public Security Bureau, was promoted to county chief of Suining, the vacant position has been concurrently held by County Chief Cheng Ruji under provincial order for many months. It is now learned that the provincial order has appointed Hua Shijun, a local resident, as the chief of the county Public Security Bureau. Hua is currently the chief of the First Branch Bureau of Public Security in this county. After receiving the order, he is scheduled to report to the bureau on the 6th and take the oath of office on a set date.

Chongming: Organization of Disaster Relief Corps in Xideyi Village, Fourth District

When the hurricane struck the river mouth, Chongming was the first to bear the brunt. On the third day of the eighth month of the Yisi year of the Guangxu reign [1905], the tidal wave at the end of the great flood had already caused a major disaster. This year, both tidal waves occurred at the beginning of the great flood. The coastal embankments have been repeatedly eroded by waves and suffered heavier damage. The destruction of houses and agricultural products is even more difficult to count. Thanks to the benevolent gentlemen at sea and various charitable organizations who have raised donations and provided food to help our compatriots. Their benevolence is truly admirable. However, it is important to remember that emergency relief can only alleviate hunger and cold for a short time, and a fundamental plan is needed for repairing embankments. The technical director of the county government estimates that the cost of construction around the perimeter is more than 500,000 yuan. After this major disaster, the people's strength is definitely not enough to bear it. The Maritime Relief Association has been established, calling out loudly, and there will surely be a response. However, even if a large sum of money is raised, it must be allocated to various counties and cannot be exclusively used for Chongming. The scale of the project is so large, and the money is so difficult to obtain. Thinking about the future, I cannot help but shudder. Qingmu returned home yesterday, and the villagers eagerly asked how to deal with the aftermath. He told them that the current emergency relief, in addition to the county relief association, relies on the continuous supply from the Sino-Foreign Relief Association. Although there is no certainty about raising funds for work relief, it must be done, like resisting the enemy, with no retreat. The elders were pleased and comforted when they heard this, and took the opportunity to propose organizing a disaster relief corps within the scope of Deyi Village, selecting 200 able-bodied men to assist in the construction of embankments along the north and south coasts. All expenses will be raised by the village itself. After discussion, everyone agreed. If the areas in Chongming that have not been affected by the tidal surge are divided into 30 groups, 6,000 people can be obtained, which would be of some help to the progress of the embankment project. This is what is meant by Chongming people helping Chongming people, and Chongming people assisting Chongming people. Only with this spirit of self-help and mutual assistance will we not fail the great philanthropists at home and abroad who are saving and helping us. Qingmu has more to say: land is immovable property, but Chongming is constantly eroding, making it no different from movable property. Therefore, embankment construction must ensure prevention of erosion to achieve consolidation. Qingmu has suggested full-scale erosion prevention and has petitioned the county government. He hopes that the elders and brothers will pay attention to this.

Wuxi: Policeman Flees with a Gun

The area under the jurisdiction of the Second Branch Bureau of Public Security in this county, which covers the main roads, is of important location. At about 2:00 AM the day before yesterday, the police chief Zheng Yaoqing of the bureau went out to check the posts as usual. To his surprise, he could not find the on-duty auxiliary policeman Zhao Jian at the post in front of Qitai Inn. He searched the surrounding area, but there was no trace. He then found a uniform worn by Zhao Jian and a wooden gun case in the sentry box. However, the insignia on the uniform had been torn off. Police Chief Zheng knew that the policeman had fled with the gun, and immediately reported to Wang Xiezhong, the chief of the branch bureau. After receiving the report, Wang sent patrol officers in different directions to search the roads, hotels, stations, and wharves, but to no avail. Yesterday, Chief Wang reported the information to the head bureau. Director Wu of the bureau sent Second Section Chief Cheng Du along with Wang Xiezhong to the Second Branch Bureau for a detailed investigation. It was found that two wooden gun cases and one pistol were missing from the armory. At 1:00 PM, Chief Cheng, accompanied by Wang Xiezhong and Sun Zhongjie, an official of the branch bureau, returned to the bureau to report. Director Wu kept Wang and Sun at the bureau for questioning and appointed Chief Cheng to temporarily take over the duties of the Second Branch Bureau. According to Wang Xiezhong, the guns had been missing from the armory for three days, but he had not reported it because he was in the process of investigation. The armory is next to the employees' room. The police officer in charge of the armory is Yu Wenhao, who has been serving for many years and also handles telephone duties on weekdays, and sleeps in the telephone room at night. The armory is only locked and not guarded, so no one knows how the guns were stolen. He also requested punishment. Director Wu then summoned police chief Zheng Yaoqing and Yu Wenhao, the police officer in charge of the armory, to the bureau and had them guarded by the special service squad. It was also discovered that the escaped policeman Zhao Jian had sent a package to the home of Qiao Liu at the Laohu Zao in Zhongzheng Road the day before yesterday afternoon. Therefore, the police were dispatched to search Qiao's house and found the package. Six suspects, including Qiao Liu, Qiao Shoulang, Xu Xiaoguizi, Bai San, Wu Xu, and Qiu Shunzao, were brought to the bureau for interrogation. It is also reported that Zhao Jian is from Jiading, 28 years old, and had just started working at the bureau two weeks ago after being introduced by Official Sun, who also acted as his guarantor.

Nantong: Three Counties Urge Zhang Xianyi to Stay

Zhang Xianyi, the chief of the Fourth District of the Jiangsu Provincial Water Police, was recently ordered to wait for reassignment before the reorganization of the Jiangsu Provincial Government, and Chi Yaozhong was appointed to succeed him. The party, government, business, and public organizations in the counties of Tong, Ru, and Hai, appreciating his service, have sent urgent telegrams to the provincial government and departments to urge his retention. Excerpts from several telegrams are listed below.

Telegram from the Nantong County Fishermen's Association to the Zhenjiang branch and the Civil Affairs Department of the Provincial Government: "Our district's maritime bandits rely on Chief Zhang of the Fourth District of the Provincial Public Security Bureau for effective suppression and are loved by the people. This time, the maritime bandit leader Jiang Si was captured, and the ships and loot were recovered, which is heartening. We have heard of his transfer and feel as if we have been deprived of our parents. We are willing to have him sit in town to deter the bandits. Please withdraw the order. We await your command."

Telegram from the Nantong County Party Headquarters: "Since Chief Zhang Xianyi of the Fourth District of the Water Police took office, he has been effective in defense and suppression, and the security of the waterways is deeply reliant on him. We are alarmed by the news of his replacement, and the public is bewildered. We hereby urgently request the withdrawal of the order to comply with public opinion."

Telegram from the Public Organizations of Rugao: "Since Chief Zhang of the Fourth District of the Water Police took office, he has disciplined the army and led his subordinates. The territory is peaceful and the people are safe. We are horrified to hear of his transfer. Please withdraw the order to reassure the people."

Telegram from the Nantong County Chamber of Commerce: "Since Chief Zhang of the Fourth District of the Water Police took office, he has strictly suppressed maritime bandits, and the banditry has been slightly quelled. Chief Zhang is upright, brave, strict, and fair. He is attentive to the order and defense of the waterways. The people of all counties love and support him. We are alarmed by the news of his transfer. We hereby urgently request commendation to encourage others."

Telegram from the Public Organizations of Haimen: "Since Chief Zhang of the Fourth District of the Water Police took office, he has spared no effort in reorganizing the defenses. Especially in the suppression of maritime bandits, he has personally faced dangers, so that the bandit nests in the Daan and Lingdian ports along the coast of our county, which have existed for many years, have been cleared once and for all, and the locality has been peaceful. We are alarmed by the news of his transfer to the province. Please comply with public opinion and quickly withdraw the order. We await your command."

Local News

The New Municipal Building in the City Center: Completion Ceremony to Be Held on Double Tenth Festival; Grand Ceremony Followed by Mayor Wu's Military Review; City Government Decides to Move to New Location on New Year's Day Next Year

The new municipal building of the Shanghai Municipal Government in the city center has been completed and is scheduled to hold its completion ceremony at 10:00 AM on the Double Tenth Festival [October 10th]. The municipal government will move in on New Year's Day next year. Details are as follows:

The New Municipal Building

The municipal government is located in the center of the city, between Fudongnei Road and Fuxinei Road. The entire project and interior decoration have been completed. The architectural model of the municipal government is an ancient palace. The lower level has four doors, and the circular beams can be followed.

Follow it straight up to the second floor. The stone steps on the left and right hang down like ribbons, with the city flower and the three characters of the Municipal Government engraved in the middle. Below the ring-shaped cave is the entrance to the ground floor. An elevator is installed here. The entire building is golden yellow, interspersed with red and green. The colors are elegant, quiet, and solemn, giving it a distinctly antique flavor. The painted buildings soar, the eaves are high and extended, beautiful and magnificent, and extremely spectacular. Entering the room and ascending the hall, the interior layout is seen, which incorporates the advantages of both Chinese and Western styles. The window frames and doors use Western styles, while the carved beams and painted walls are purely ancient Chinese rules. The auditorium on the third floor is particularly colorful, with a green painted ceiling, grand and gorgeous. The mayor's office is on the east side of the auditorium, and the secretary-general's office is on the west side. The rest are the secretariat and office of various departments on the second floor. The lower level has a reception room, a conference room, and a cafeteria. The top floor is used as a storage room and a rest room for the police. Below the front eaves, a firm plaque bears the words "Municipal Government." The surroundings have observation decks. The outer circle of the new building is surrounded by grass, which has also been completely arranged, with green grass and small flowers interspersed with flower beds. In front of the gate of the municipal government, flagpoles stand tall on the left and right, ready for hanging the party and national flags. The square corner lights along the road are silver with gold-yellow copper edges, which complement the color scheme of the new municipal building and are also extremely spectacular. Behind the new building, only separated by a road, is the bronze statue of Sun Yat-sen. The base has been completed. If it can be rushed, it will be moved there on the 10th. Behind it is the Sun Yat-sen Memorial Hall, which has begun the foundation filling. The two municipal museums and libraries that the municipal government is currently building will be located on the left and right sides of the memorial hall in the future.

A Glimpse of the Bureaus

The office buildings of the bureaus are the same as the original architectural plan of the new municipal building, but on a smaller scale. Due to the impact of the January 28th Incident [Shanghai Incident], financial constraints, and the lack of time, temporary office buildings were built for the bureaus. They have now all been completed. The Bureau of Land and the Bureau of Public Works are combined into one office, located to the east of the government. The Bureau of Social Affairs, Education, and Health are in one office, located to the west of the municipal government. The Bureau of Finance and the Bureau of Public Utilities are temporarily located in the new municipal building. They will be moved after the new buildings of the bureaus are built. The Public Security Bureau is still located in the Nanshi area and will be moved to the old site of the Shanghai County Government on January 1st next year when the bureaus are relocated. As for the police affairs in the city center, a new office of the Second Sub-Bureau of the Seventh District of the Public Security Bureau has been built on Qimei Road, which is larger than other police stations. After the municipal government moves in in the future, police forces will be expanded to maintain the security of the city center.

Grand Ceremony

The ceremony will be held from 10:00 AM to about 12:00 PM on October 10th. A. New building completion ceremony: play music, raise the flag, fire cannons, play music, open the gate, unveil the memorial tablet, perform the ceremony (in the auditorium), report, play music, military review, ceremony complete. The military review will be around 11:00 AM. In addition to the military review passing in front of the new municipal building, there will also be Boy Scouts, fire brigades, vehicles, and the national goods parade team. B. The fire brigade will perform in front of the new municipal building, around 2:00 PM.

Mayor's Military Review

The military review ceremony will be held around 11:00 AM. Participants include the First and Second Regiments of the Security Bureau, which will be temporarily formed into one regiment, as well as the vehicle patrol team and pistol team directly under the Security Bureau, totaling about 2,000 people. In addition to the police brigade, the Public Security Bureau will also draw more than 1,000 police officers from various districts. The local defense groups from various districts will also participate on this day. The total number of people is about 4,000 to 5,000. Mayor Wu will personally review them.

Firefighting Demonstration

There are about 25 firefighting vehicles. They must be parked on Shizheng Tong Road before 9:00 AM, at the fire brigade parking signs, such as West Sports Association Road, Xiangyin Road, Songhu Road, Sanmin Road, in front of the new municipal building, Fuxian Zuolu, Funei Road, Guowei Road, and Shizheng Tong Road. After the military review, they will follow the Boy Scouts, passing in front of the new municipal building, turning into Shizheng Tong Road, Songhu Road, Sanmin Road, in front of the new municipal building, Fuxian Zuolu, Funei Road, Guowei Road, and Shizheng Tong Road. During the performance at 2:00 PM, the route will still be Shizheng Tong Road, Songhu Road, Sanmin Road, in front of the new municipal building.

Motorcade Parade

The national goods parade motorcade has about 45 vehicles. At around 11:00 AM, they will drive to the intersection of Xiangyin Road and Qimei Road to park. During the military review, they will follow the fire brigade vehicles, passing in front of the new municipal building. The route is as follows: West Sports Association Road, Xiangyin Road, Qimei Road intersection (stop), turn into Songhu Road during the military review, Sanmin Road, in front of the new municipal building, Fuxian Zuolu, Funei Road, Guowei Road, Xiangyin Road, Qimei Road, Disiwei Road.

Traffic Routes

The traffic routes and parking locations for visitors have been stipulated. A. Visitors' cars: (upward) Park Target Practice Field, West Sports Association Road, Xiangyin Road, Songhu Road, Sanmin Road, in front of the new municipal building; (downward) in front of the new municipal building, Fuxian Zuolu, Funei Road, Guowei Road, Xiangyin Road, Qimei Road, Disiwei Road (or Huangxing Road, Ningguo Road, Huade Road). B. Cars for picking up and dropping off guests (renting Xiang Sheng Car Company rental cars, with a Chinese flag on the radiator cap), guests can ride for free with a viewing ticket: (upward) same as A; (downward) in front of the new municipal building, Fuxian Zuolu, Funei Road, Guowei Road, Xiangyin Road, Qimei Road, Disiwei Road, Park Target Practice Field. C. Shanghai Chinese Public Bus Company will operate 10 special buses (single trip 20 cents per person): (upward) Baoshan Road intersection, West Sports Ground Road, Xiangyin Road, Songhu Road, Sanmin Road, Fuxian Youlu; (downward) Fuxian Youlu, Funei Road, Guowei Road, Xiangyin Road, West Sports Ground Road, Baoshan Road. D. Routes for marching groups (after 8:00 AM): (1) (upward) Laobazi Road, East Sports Ground Road, Xiangyin Road, Funan Youlu, military review ground in front of the municipal government; (afternoon) military review ground, Funan Youlu, Xiangyin Road, East Sports Ground Road, Laobazi Road. (2) Jiangwan, Xiangyin Road, Funan Youlu, military review ground in front of the municipal government.

Seven Decorated Arches

Due to the completion ceremony of the new municipal building in the city center, decorated arches were hastily built yesterday. A bell-shaped decorated arch, 30 feet high, was built at the intersection of Xiangyin Road, Qimei Road, and Songhu Road, the three roads from the Concession entering the city center. One arch at the eastern entrance and exit of Xiangyin Road, one arch at the eastern entrance and exit of Qimei Road, one arch at the intersection of Sanmin Road, one arch at the intersection of Jungong Road, one arch at the intersection of Wuquan Road, and one arch each on Fudongnei Road and Fuxinei Road, shaped like Yuanmen, totaling seven arches. They are all decorated with colorful cypress branches and adorned with fresh flowers, with horizontal plaques bearing the words "Completion Ceremony of the City Center." A five-story building made of bamboo poles and reed mats has been built in the city center as a demonstration for the firefighters. This hypothetical five-story building is built in front of the new municipal building.

Aviation Administration Cables: Nine Aircraft Will Fly Around the City on the Double Tenth Festival to Promote National Attention to Aviation; All Shanghai Aircraft Arrived in Shanghai on the 9th

The Chinese Aviation Association received a reply from Xu Peigen, director of the Hangzhou Aviation Administration, stating, "Aviation Association: Approved your letter requesting to send aircraft to Shanghai to distribute leaflets. Song Ziwen Discusses: Customs Bonds to Repay Old Debts; Chen Guangfu Appointed Chairman of Cotton Control Association; National Economic Council to Set Up Office in Shanghai

After returning to Shanghai from the Finance Department office on West Yanan Road yesterday morning with League of Nations Commissioner Rajchman, Finance Minister Song Ziwen met with reporters from various newspapers at 10:00 AM yesterday morning and strongly denied the rumor that 100 million yuan of new customs bonds would be used to borrow 50 million yuan from the banking community first. Song's remarks are recorded below.

Bond Lending is Incorrect

Song said first, "The rumor that the Ministry of Finance's issuance of 100 million yuan of customs bonds will be used to borrow 50 million yuan from the banking community is not true. These bonds will be used entirely to repay arrears and have been negotiated in advance. In the past five or six months, the Ministry of Finance has borrowed more than 60 million yuan from the banking community. Most of these loans are temporary. At this time, we must first repay these debts."

Strive for Balanced Revenue and Expenditure

Although the central government's finances are currently extremely tight, we are trying to find a way to overcome this difficulty. The first issue is to ensure that revenue and expenditure are balanced. For military spending, for example, in North China it has been reduced from more than 7 million yuan to 4.5 million yuan. In the future, central military spending will also have to be reduced. However, the central armies are currently working hard to suppress bandits. In fact, this is not yet possible.

Cotton Association to be Established Soon

The Cotton Control Association of the National Economic Council is now ready and can be established within days. The committee will consist of about a dozen people. Chen Guangfu, Tang Xinghai, Li Shengbo, Zou Bingwen, Xie Qi, and others have been hired. Chen will be the director. The remaining committee members are still being sought. In the future, all expenses will be allocated by the government to the greatest extent.

Various Associations Organized Step by Step

The organization of other committees such as silk, mining, and food will also not be delayed and will be carried out step by step. The government intends to hire people with extensive experience in each industry to serve as the heads of these associations, while the government will assist from the sidelines as a backing. However, the government will be particularly cautious about all personnel matters to avoid being manipulated.

Office to be Established in Shanghai

For the convenience of handling matters, the National Economic Council has decided to set up an office in Shanghai and is currently looking for a building. Once it is selected, it can be established. The Engineering Office of the National Economic Council will be renamed the Water Conservancy Office and will be moved to Nanjing soon. The promotion of American cotton and American wheat will still be managed by the Office for Purchasing American Cotton and Wheat, which is affiliated with the Central Bank. Rajchman is the League of Nations' special liaison for technical cooperation in China and is under the National Economic Council, supervising the technical personnel sent to China by the League of Nations. There are more technical personnel coming to China after Rajchman. The League of Nations will be notified to send them again depending on the need for technical personnel. There is no need for Rajchman to set up an office himself.

Reciprocal Tariffs Not Detailed

I am afraid it is just talk, or it may be a propaganda effort on their part."

The Flour Industry Association Discussed Relief Measures Yesterday, and the Flour Exchange Suspended Trading Yesterday

The Flour Mill Association of this city, in view of the gradual decline of the domestic flour industry and the recent downturn that threatens to shut down all flour mills in Shanghai, held a public meeting at the Banking Club yesterday at 5:00 PM. Representatives from Fuxin, Fufeng, Huafeng, Xinda Xiang, Xin Zhonghua, Shenda, and other mills, totaling more than ten people, attended. Gu Xin-yi was elected as chairman. The chairman gave a report, stating that the flour mill industry has been declining in recent years, reaching an extreme point, hence the convening of the meeting to discuss relief strategies. Representatives from various mills then described the sluggish sales of flour and the daily decline in flour prices, with the selling price per bag not covering costs, especially for lower-grade flour, which had no sales at all. Since the loss of Northeast China, a major sales area for flour, the flour mill industry has suffered a major blow. Furthermore, Tianjin has been flooded with foreign flour, and foreign flour transactions have continued recently. Although the Chinese government has increased import taxes by more than one dime per bag, it is regrettably too light. With the recent depreciation of foreign exchange rates, this small tax is not enough to deter dumping. Therefore, sales in the Beiyang gang (Tianjin gang) cannot be restored, while the Nanyang gang, such as Fuzhou and Xiamen, are plagued by soldiers and bandits, and merchants dare not purchase and transport goods. The exchange market is deserted by long positions, causing the market to decline further. Therefore, it is necessary to gradually suspend work as a passive relief measure. Subsequently, six resolutions were passed: (1) The import tariff on foreign flour should be increased by another one to five dimes, as Japan's import tax on foreign flour is about one yuan, and the import tax on Little Luzon is about five dimes. (2) Please allocate 10 million yuan from the cotton and wheat loan, lend it out at a low interest rate, and repay it in installments. (3) Please organize a national food control committee through the National Economic Council as soon as possible. (4) Small-scale mechanized flour mills in the interior should be subject to the same unified tax as the factories. (5) Reduce flour transportation costs. (6) National military supplies should purchase flour from various factories as much as possible to reduce inventory.

In addition, the Shanghai Flour Exchange suddenly suspended trading yesterday. Due to the daily decline of the flour industry, the price of flour has fallen sharply, requiring short positions to increase margin calls. The amount to be added reached more than 300,000 yuan, but only more than 100,000 yuan has been added, with a large portion still unpaid. Therefore, trading was suspended. If the margin call is not fully paid today, trading will be suspended again.

Shipping Merchants Held a General Meeting Yesterday, Requesting That Water-Land Intermodal Transport Include Private Ships

The Ministry of Railways and the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company (CMSNC) signed a national railway-water intermodal transport contract. Before the contract was signed, Yu Qiaqing of the Sanbei Company telegraphed the ministry, requesting that the operating rights of private shipping lines be taken into consideration. The Ministry of Railways replied that the intermodal transport contract signed by the Railway Administration and the CMSNC was also a preliminary trial measure. Later, Yu sent another telegram, arguing that intermodal transport should not be exclusive to one company and that the establishment of the program should be carefully considered, taking all factors into account to ensure fairness. After this telegram was sent, a reply was received from the ministry, stating that it was difficult to comply with the inclusion of private shipping companies in intermodal transport. Upon receiving this news, Shanghai shipping merchants rose up in opposition, arguing that the transportation of state-owned railways being exclusive to CMSNC would leave other shipping companies with no business. Therefore, yesterday at 3:00 PM, the Shanghai Shipping Association convened an emergency general meeting of all private shipping companies at No. 10 Guangdong Road, where each company sent responsible representatives to discuss breaking the monopoly of water-land intermodal transport and fighting for inclusion, in order to determine a course of action. Around 3:00 PM, representatives from various shipping companies (excluding CMSNC) arrived at the meeting one after another. Yu Qiaqing, Chen Bogang, and representative Le Zhenbao, and other members of the executive committee of the Shanghai Shipping Association first discussed many precedents. Then, they proposed that the railway-water intermodal transport contract signed by the Ministry of Railways and the CMSNC for all national railway lines, especially the freight transport of the Longhai Railway, was particularly important. Once implemented, companies such as Dazhen and Hezhong would have no cargo to transport. They discussed this for a long time, generally agreeing that the opposition of private shipping companies to the intermodal transport contract signed by the Ministry of Railways was not against CMSNC monopolizing the profits, but rather against the Ministry of Railways not taking into account the majority of shipping companies and rashly assigning the freight transport of all national railway lines to one company. Regardless of whether CMSNC's tonnage was insufficient

to meet the demand, it was unfair to deprive the majority of shipping companies of the same treatment of state-owned railway transportation. The entire body unanimously decided to petition the Ministry of Railways again, requesting that private merchant ships be included in the water-land intermodal transport contract and that no single company should monopolize it. After the decision was made, the shipping association drafted a document in the name of all shipping companies, strongly protesting to the Ministry of Railways.

News of the Electrical Workers' Strike Yesterday, Shanghai Chamber of Commerce Issued a Declaration Yesterday

Regarding the strike by workers at the Shanghai Power Company, workers in various departments continued to slow down work, and some left the factory. A reporter from the Xinsheng News Agency made separate investigations at various locations yesterday and was given a statement by the vice president and general manager of the Power Company, Mr. Xierde, as follows:

For the Pension Fund

Mr. Xierde told the reporter from the Xinsheng News Agency that the workers at the new factory of the Shanghai Power Company on Dongting Road, in protest against the company's dismissal of three workers, slowed down work on the morning of the 29th of last month. On the 2nd of this month, they joined the workers at the old factory on Feilun Road and left the factory to strike at the same time. The day before yesterday, temporary workers at the new factory and foremen at the old factory also joined the strike. Because the company refused to pay the pension, 1,400 striking workers from the new and old factories continued their strike yesterday. The remaining 1,100 people, such as the staff in the office and the electricity generation workers in the new and old factories, continued to work as usual.

Handling According to Contract

He also stated that of the three workers dismissed, two had been of bad character and one had been at fault and had voluntarily resigned. According to the contract signed between the company and the Municipal Council, they could not be paid. Moreover, since the company was not at fault, it could not violate its established regulations in order to meet the workers' additional demands. It was found that the strike by the workers at the two factories was instigated by others, and the labor side's claim that the company sent police to prevent workers from entering and leaving was purely fabricated.

Unfavorable Temptation

According to reports, the Power Company has always treated the labor union very well. However, due to the instigation of unscrupulous elements, many good workers were intimidated and unable to work. The company regrets this. There are many good workers working in the factory who have asked the company to ask the police for protection and to live and eat in the factory for fear of disturbance by the striking workers. This shows that the workers' intentions are not unified.

Power Generation Unhindered

The reporter also asked what the company would do if the power generation workers and staff joined the strike. According to the reply, this had not been heard before. However, as a public utility, for the sake of serving society, if it came to this point, the company would definitely hire other workers to replace them. Moreover, Shanghai relies entirely on electricity for factories such as electrical machinery factories and flour mills. For the convenience of business and the needs of all sectors, even if all three shifts of workers went on strike, the company would definitely recruit workers to keep the electricity flowing. Therefore, power generation will not be a problem. As for the striking workers, if they want to enter the factory to work, the company will still allow them to continue to serve. The line cutters who have returned to work are actually workers who voluntarily came to the factory to work.

Foremen's Meeting

The Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs attached great importance to this case and had sent personnel to mediate with the Municipal Party Department several times without success. Fearing that the situation would further escalate, they sent a special report to the Municipal Government yesterday to request a review and handling so that the dispute could be resolved as soon as possible. In addition, the Water and Electricity Workers' Union of the Fourth District, because the workers have been away from the factory for many days and the problem has not been resolved, decided to hold a foremen's meeting at 3:00 PM on the 8th to discuss countermeasures.

Chamber of Commerce Declaration

The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce issued a declaration regarding the Shanghai Power Company's dismissal of workers and the capital side's failure to comply with government regulations and mediation, which has led to the expansion of the situation and hindered public utilities. The Chamber of Commerce, taking a fair stance, issued a special declaration stating that the Shanghai Power Company had repeatedly experienced disputes over the dismissal of workers such as Ni Genfu and the payment of pension funds. The Party Department and the Chinese directors of the Municipal Council had mediated several times without success. On September 27, the company suddenly dismissed Xue A'bao, Dai Renheng, Yin Binggen, and others without paying their pension funds, causing all the workers at the new factory to declare a slowdown on the 29th. Later, because the factory refused the workers' demands and forced the dismissed workers to be dismissed altogether, the workers at the old factory rose up in support, and the situation further escalated. The Chamber of Commerce believes that labor-capital disputes can be resolved legally, but the company, due to its national status, refused to comply with the government's legal mediation, resulting in a prolonged stalemate. It seems that the company has not taken into account the position of public utilities and the importance of labor-capital cooperation, which cannot but be regretted. Therefore, a declaration is specially issued as follows, hoping to arouse the company's attention:

Company Notice

The company issued a notice to the workers yesterday, stating that many incorrect statements have recently been found in the newspapers in this city. The company has no choice but to describe the facts in detail to avoid being misled by false statements. (1) The 5% worker pension fund previously issued during the Municipal Council era has now been reduced to 1% or 2%. Furthermore, the company can arbitrarily cancel this reduced pension fund. For dismissed workers, the company can falsely claim that the workers were dismissed due to misconduct, and the pension fund can be refused. The correct facts are as follows: When the company was not separated from the Municipal Council, employees who had worked for 20 years or more were given a severance payment regardless of the reason for their departure, calculated at 5% of their annual salary per year of service. However, those who left before 20 years of service were not entitled to this right. This was an extra bonus to the salary, and the intention was to encourage employees to cooperate with the company. Therefore, the company agreed to accept this method and continue to implement it. Later, the company, together with the Municipal Council, revised the severance payment regulations. According to the company's method, employees who have worked for 15 years or more will be given a severance payment of 5% of their annual salary per year of service, regardless of the reason for leaving the job. In addition, employees who have worked for less than 15 years and are dismissed by the company not due to their own fault will also be given the severance payment proportionally according to their length of service. Except for these regulations, no severance payment will be given. Employees who have worked for less than 15 years and are dismissed by the company due to their own fault, or because they are not diligent in their service, or because they sleep during work, or because they are arrested for leaving their posts without authorization, will not be able to enjoy this severance payment. These employees, whether in the Municipal Council era or in the company era, cannot enjoy the severance payment. The company has never violated the above-mentioned regulations. Worker Xue A'bao took sick leave on September 13 this time. His condition was examined by a Chinese doctor, and because it was suspicious, the doctor suggested that only two days of sick leave should be given. Xue returned to the factory on September 15 and stated that his illness had fully recovered. However, after September 15, Xue left again and did not go to work. On the morning of September 25, Xue went to the Yangshupu factory sign room and claimed that he had to resign and asked the company to calculate his salary. However, when the salary was handed over for him to sign, Xue refused to receive it because the above-mentioned severance payment was not paid together. Employee Dai Renheng left his work place without authorization and was dismissed. Employee Zhou Binggen left his work place and slept during work and was dismissed. Obviously, none of the above can enjoy the severance payment. Also, the company did not receive prior notice of this strike, and the two representatives never met with the company authorities. Zhuang Songfu Plans to Establish the Zhejiang Provincial Fishermen's Autonomous Federation, He Passed Through Shanghai from Hangzhou Yesterday and Talked About It

Zhuang Songfu of the Zhejiang Provincial Autonomous Committee went to Zhenhai, Xiangshan, Yin County, Cixi, etc. last month to investigate the local autonomy situation. After returning to the province, he expressed some views on the Zhejiang Provincial Autonomy Plan. Yesterday, Zhuang passed through Shanghai from Hangzhou and took the Hongxing ship to Yong, then to Nantian and Ninghai counties to investigate autonomy. Zhuang told visitors yesterday that he recently plans to establish a Zhejiang Provincial Fishermen's Autonomous Federation. The people on land have autonomy, and the people on the water may also have autonomous groups. Now, fishermen are being robbed by pirates and exploited by fishermen and merchants, which is becoming increasingly bankrupt. The reasons are: (1) Fishermen are not united. When one ship encounters thieves, other ships avoid and do not help, relying on fate and not thinking about remedies. (2) The fishing boats and fishermen of each gang are of uneven quality. They are not inspected at ordinary times, so thief ships are mixed among them, and no one interferes. (3) Fishermen do not have a joint organization, so there is no fixed price regulation in terms of sales, and it is monopolized by fishermen and merchants. The above reasons are the fundamental reasons for the direct damage suffered by fishermen. Therefore, it is planned to establish a fishermen's autonomous federation, with five blood ships compiled as a row, ten rows compiled as a class, and each gang compiled as a risk. Each team has an office, and the offices are jointly formed into a general autonomous group. The group will establish fishermen's self-defense corps, production and marketing cooperatives, etc., so that they can help each other from beginning to end and form a cohesive whole, which is the fundamental method to maintain the fishery. If this proposal can be adopted, it is planned to start in Zhejiang Province first.

CMSNC Leases Three Seaships and Cancels

The state-run China Merchants Steam Navigation Company (CMSNC) leased the Pu'an ship from the Ministry of the Navy to operate jointly, traveling between Qingdao and Putuo. Since July 17th this summer, the three-month term expired on the 16th of last month and operations were suspended. The CMSNC responded to the requests from all parties and decided to discuss with the Ministry of the Navy to continue the lease. In order to expand its business, it planned to rent the Jing'an and Ke'an ships at the same time. However, the Ministry of the Navy planned to sell the Jing'an to the Sanbei Company, and the price had been agreed upon. Therefore, the CMSNC's plan was difficult to implement. Now, the CMSNC has received a letter from the Ministry of the Navy stating that the Pu'an ship has other uses and will be taken back. The Ke'an ship is also too deep in draft, and the CMSNC's docking at the wharf after leasing it would be very difficult, so it is not planned to lease it alone. The bureau's three-ship lease plan with the Ministry of the Navy has been completely cancelled.

Key News on Disaster Relief for the Southern Sichuan Flood

Two hurricanes were discovered last month, causing significant damage to coastal counties, especially Chuansha and Nanhui counties, which were the most severely affected. Therefore, disaster relief efforts have been quite busy. Key news is recorded as follows:

Mu Jichu and Others Arrive in Chuansha to Inspect

Mu Jichu, Zou Bingwen (represented by Ye Yuanding), Xu Jishi, inspectors of the Shanghai Pudong Storm and Flood Disaster Relief Committee, and Shen Zijian of the Pudong Fellow-Provincials Association, arrived in Chuansha from Shanghai at 10:00 AM on September 29th. After lunch, County Magistrate Li Leng and Cui Xilin, a member of the disaster relief committee, accompanied them to inspect the disaster situation along the coast of the fourth and fifth districts. According to Mu, the disaster situation in Chuansha County was indeed more severe than in Nanhui County. After returning to the committee and reporting, it was decided that clothing, rice, and other relief supplies would be provided continuously. Because Mu and others had other important matters, they were unable to inspect Hengsha and other places. They returned to Shanghai by long-distance bus at 9:00 AM the next morning.

Third Committee Meeting Convened

The third committee meeting was held at 10:00 AM on the same day. In addition to reporting items, the most important of the discussed items were (1) to distribute the cotton clothing purchased by the committee to the disaster victims in the fourth and fifth districts. Four committee members, including Lu Rong'an, were assigned to work with the district heads to handle this. As for the cotton clothing for the disaster victims in the sixth district, a telegram was sent to the Shanghai Pudong Storm and Flood Disaster Relief Committee to allocate it quickly. (2) The Shanghai Pudong Storm and Flood Disaster Relief Committee delivered 260 bags of relief rice during the meeting. It was immediately decided to allocate 140 bags to the fourth and fifth districts and 120 bags to the sixth district, to be managed by the district offices. Six committee members, including Xue Songgan, were assigned to supervise the process.

Two Health Teams Arrive in Chuansha to Work

Furthermore, the health team sent by the Relief Committee, totaling 18 doctors and nurses, arrived in Chuansha at 1:00 PM on October 1st. They were divided into two teams. One team of eight people was stationed in Bailonggang Town in the fifth district, and the other team of ten people was stationed on Gaodunsha Island in the sixth district. Zhu, the general affairs director of the disaster relief committee, and Yu, the chief inspector of the public security bureau, took care of them. After dinner, the team stationed in Bailonggang was sent to their destination by hired car on the same day. The team stationed on Gaodunsha Island stayed overnight in the city due to ferry connections and were sent by hired car the next day. With these saviors, the lives of the disaster victims should be secure.

Relief Home Requests Sustained Charitable Acts

The Xinwei Relief Association of this city received a telegram from Xu Naibing, Chuan Zuoheng, and others of the Nanhui County Relief Home, requesting continued support and assistance. The original telegram is recorded as follows: To the esteemed Xinwei Relief Association: Nanhui has been hit by two hurricanes, and along the coast, from Sanzao in the fourth district in the south to Qituan in the second district in the north, about seven miles long, more than 20 sections of dikes have been destroyed. The water is deep and submerging, and houses have been turned into ruins. The plight of the disaster victims has been reported in detail by County Magistrate Yuan and investigators from Shanghai charitable organizations. We are extremely grateful that major philanthropists have raised funds for emergency relief. However, this year's extraordinary disaster has not only affected coastal residents, but also the Relief Home. The Relief Home has approximately 18,000 mu of land, all located in the Ligongtang area along the coast. We rely entirely on collecting rent to maintain the annual operating expenses of 30,000 yuan. This year, we have been repeatedly affected by windstorms, and the Ligongtang dikes have been destroyed. The Relief Home's land has been the first to bear the brunt, and a vast expanse has become a swamp. This year's rent is not to be expected. Then, from where will come the funds for the current reformatory, old-age home, orphanage, women's shelter, orphanage, and monthly external care programs? If we want to stop, the livelihood of thousands of helpless poor people will be cut off. If we want to maintain, we have no way to borrow the huge sum of 30,000 yuan. We are in a dilemma, with no good solution. In addition to sending telegrams to various charitable organizations to seek relief, we hereby send a telegram to your esteemed association, requesting that you treat us equally and consider us at the same time, and provide us with appropriate assistance to maintain charitable acts. We are eagerly awaiting your instructions. Xu Naibing, Chuan Zuoheng, Ji Difan, Yang Binru, Zhao Xinmei, Pan Kejun, Zhang Jianqian, Pan Ziping, and Xia Chuankun of the Nanhui County Relief Home kowtow together.

Jianghai Customs Adjusts Export Tariff on Waste Wool

The Jianghai Customs issued a notice yesterday stating: Now, following the instructions of the Customs Administration of the Ministry of Finance, the tax collection methods for all waste goat wool and waste cashmere wool transported abroad should be adjusted as follows: (1) For waste goat wool containing no more than 10% cashmere wool, tax should be levied according to item 176 of the export tariff. (2) For waste goat wool containing more than 10% cashmere wool but worth no more than 30 yuan per dan, tax should still be levied according to item 176 of the export tariff. (3) For waste goat wool containing more than 10% cashmere wool and worth more than 30 yuan per dan, tax should be levied according to item 188 of the export tariff. The above methods will be implemented from October 4th of this year. All merchants should be informed. This is hereby announced. October 5, 1933, Ning Huaian, Supervisor; Bolaisen, Customs Commissioner.
