Requests from Two Hospitals for Increased Subsidies and Tax Exemption Submitted to the Municipal Council for Discussion

The Shanghai Sanitarium and Health Hospital requested the Municipal Council to increase its annual subsidy by 5,000 taels in addition to the existing 5,000 taels due to increased treatment costs. According to the Director of Finance, it would not be convenient to increase the subsidy this year, but it could be considered next year. After deliberation by the Finance Committee, it was proposed that the subsidy should not be increased this year. If the hospital provides a detailed explanation of the situation, it could be considered in detail in next year's budget. This proposal was adopted by the Board of Directors on October 3rd.

The newly established Shanghai Mental Hospital requested that its address, Nos. 22-26, Lane 208, Kuling Road, be exempted from municipal taxes because the hospital is maintained by charitable donations and provides free treatment, and is recognized by the local court. According to reports from the Tax Bureau and the Health Department, the annual tax amount for this address is 675.50 yuan. However, the nature of the building is not suitable for severely ill patients and is prone to fire hazards. However, the hospital's work in receiving patients delivered by the court is necessary, and the Municipal Council's mental hospital has not yet been established. It seems that a tax exemption can be granted, but the Fire Department and the Health Department should supervise it at any time, and the matter should be reconsidered after six months. After reconsideration by the Finance Committee, it was proposed to approve the request. This proposal has been adopted by the Board of Directors.

—Court Approves Withdrawal of Charges—

Yao Xiaoyong Commits Suicide

Yao Xiaoyong, a local resident, 26 years old, went to Room 15 of the Xiangxing Small Inn on Baliqiao Road in the French Concession at around 1:00 AM last night. Due to misappropriation of disaster relief funds, which caused trouble for the guarantor, he felt a sudden pang of conscience and had the thought of death. He secretly ingested opium paste and committed suicide. After being discovered by the teahouse, he was sent to Renji Hospital by car. The treatment was ineffective, and he died at around 4:00 AM. He left a suicide note addressed to his brother, named Borong, who lived at No. 47 Changan Lane, Maite Husted Road. The content stated that since serving in the French-owned Coal Company, several years had passed in a flash. Now, the disaster relief funds were used privately and there was no way to make up for it, and he had no face to see anyone. Recently, he heard that the company had detained the guarantor in the police station to investigate the accounts, and he felt deeply uneasy about the guarantor suffering on his behalf. He was ashamed to live in the world, and he only had one death to end it all, hoping to repay his life in the next life.

Yuan Songshan, Accountant of Dingtong Company, Sentenced for Smuggling Red Pills - A Large Batch of 420 Pounds of Red Pills Seized - The Main Culprit Zhao Shancai Fled with His Entire Family in Fear of Punishment

—Yuan Songshan Sentenced to One Year of Imprisonment; Two Accomplices Sentenced to Six Months Each—

Zhao Shancai, who established a factory in the countryside west of Shanghai, specialized in manufacturing red pills and secretly transporting them for sale inland. The transportation was planned by a Mr. Yu residing at No. 33 Aidao Ya Road, a Mr. Feng residing at No. 28 Aierjin Road, and Yuan Songshan (nicknamed Yuan Shikai), an accountant from Dingtong Transportation Company on Jie Road, who was from Wuxi. They had never failed before. At 2:00 PM on the 29th of last month, Zhao and others hired Yin Zuoyu's cargo truck to drive to the border between the Chinese and French concessions, where they loaded three large boxes of red pills, intending to transport them to the North Railway Station and then by train for sale inland. However, the secret plan was discovered by Liu Junjie, an investigator from the General Inspectorate, who, along with Detective Liu Shaokui, Deputy Detective Song Bingzheng, and Ping Zhiming, waited at the bridge on North Xizang Road, which was a necessary route. They soon saw a

Cargo Truck

coming from the south and heading north at high speed. The detectives immediately ordered the truck to stop and arrested Yin, the driver Fang Ajiu, and the two workers Zhang Agen and Liu Burong, along with Yan Baoqi. Upon inspecting the boxes, they found that each box contained seven large bags of Silver Horse brand red pills, and each bag was divided into forty small bags. They took the truck back to the police station along with the arrested individuals. The total weight was 420 pounds. After interrogating Yin and others, Yin confessed that the red pills were to be delivered to Jiang Afu at the station, who was still waiting there. The detectives then took Yin to the North Station and arrested Jiang Afu. Jiang confessed that he was a

Foreman at Dingtong

and that the company's accountant, Yuan Songshan, had ordered him to load the red pills into the cargo room, so he was waiting there. The detectives then arrested Jiang and Yuan. The next morning, they were taken to the First Special District Local Court, where Judge Qian Hongye reviewed the case. Except for the driver Fang Ajiu and the three workers Zhang, Liu, and Yan, who were confirmed to be unaware that the goods being transported were prohibited drugs, they were allowed to post bail and wait for further questioning. Yin and Jiang were detained, and Yuan Songshan was released on 3,000 yuan bail, pending further investigation. Later, the investigating detectives found that the main culprit, Zhao Shancai, lived at No. 24 Julai Da Road in the French Concession. When they went to investigate the address along with detectives from the French police, they found that Zhao had already heard the news and

Fled with His Entire Family

leaving behind little furniture. After searching, they found many wrapping papers and towels. The trademark on the towels was the same as the trademark on the towels seized from the truck that was used to wrap the red pills. They then searched the residences of Mr. Yu and Mr. Feng, but only found a contract signed by Feng with the Zhongxing Coal Mine Company for transporting coal. Yesterday morning, the case was continued. The police brought the defendants to court for questioning. Judge Qian presided over the hearing. First, the police lawyer, Qian Xunjiu, explained the progress of the ongoing investigation and presented the towels, the contract, and other items as evidence. Then, the detective Liu Junjie reported the

Investigation Work

and the results he had obtained. An employee surnamed Wang from the Zhongxing Coal Mine Company also appeared in court to prove that the contract signed with Mr. Feng was for transporting coal. At this point, lawyer Qian presented another letter, stating that the police had received this letter after solving the case and that the court could understand the relationship between Dingtong Company and the case after reading it. Judge Qian then questioned the defendant Jiang Afu, but Jiang denied everything and retracted the facts he had confessed during the initial hearing, claiming ignorance. Judge Qian then read his previous statement [Yuan Songshan told me that there were several

Oriental Goods

and ordered me to load them into the cargo room, giving me one yuan per piece. A few days later, Yuan said that the goods had arrived, and I asked him what kind they were. Yuan said they were red pills and would give me one hundred yuan per box] for him to hear. Jiang then lowered his head and said nothing. The defendant Yuan Songshan also completely denied everything, saying that he was falsely accused by Jiang. However, Yin Zuoyu had previously confessed that he knew the items being loaded were red pills. Now, he suddenly recanted his confession, claiming that he did not know they were red pills at first, and only found out after the case was solved. The court had already learned the truth and immediately ordered the start of the debate. After the police lawyer and the defendants' lawyers had completed their arguments, Judge Qian sentenced Yuan Songshan to one year of imprisonment, Yin Zuoyu and Jiang Afu to six months of imprisonment each, and Fang, Zhang, Liu, and Yan were released. The red pills and other items were confiscated.

A Woman Died Tragically - Saving One Yuan through Hardship - Enduring Abuse and Humiliation, She Ended Her Life

—Mrs. Ye Can Be Said to Have Indirectly Caused the Death—

Sun Buyao, a 25-year-old Ningbo native from Fenghua, residing at No. 41 Xisanli Bridge, South Pier, Pudong, in the house of landlord Mrs. Wang Ye, worked as a carpenter. His family was very poor. His wife, Mrs. Pan, was 19 years old, and the couple had a very good relationship. However, Mrs. Pan saved some money every day when buying groceries and deposited it with the landlord, Mrs. Ye. Recently, she had accumulated a total of one silver dollar. Mrs. Ye told Sun that his wife had saved one silver dollar from her grocery money and deposited it with her, and that she would deduct this one dollar, so Sun only needed to pay back five more dollars. Sun was moved to tears by his wife's frugality. However, Mrs. Pan, knowing that Mrs. Ye should not have revealed her secret, fearing that her husband would blame and scold her, argued with Mrs. Ye. Mrs. Ye even slapped her twice. Mrs. Pan, humiliated and feeling like she did not want to live, took advantage of her husband's inattention and ran alone to the shore of the South Pier around 8:00 PM, jumping into the river to commit suicide. Because it was dark, she could not be rescued in time and drowned. Her body sank and its whereabouts are unknown. Others informed Sun, who rushed to report to the Third Precinct of the Third District. Director Dong ordered the police to summon Mrs. Ye to the station. The plaintiff claimed that although his wife did not die at Mrs. Ye's hands, Mrs. Ye caused her to seek death and requested justice. The defendant confessed that the deceased argued with her during the day and that she slapped her twice, but she did not expect her to seek death. The Director, considering the tragic circumstances of the case, ordered Sun Buyao to hire someone to find and retrieve the body for an autopsy, and also sent the plaintiff and defendant to the Local Court for questioning.

Page 16

Ferry Overloaded with Passengers - Several Female Workers Drowned - Ferryman Still Trying to Shirk Responsibility - Female Worker Appeared at the Scene to Testify

Between Xiaonanyang Wharf in Lujiazui, Pudong, and the Fair Road Wharf in Hudong across the river, there is a type of wooden ferry that specializes in carrying male and female workers who live in Pudong and work in factories such as the Nanyang Tobacco Factory in Hudong back and forth across the river. According to the regulations of the Customs, this type of ferry is only allowed to carry 30 passengers at a time. However, because workers are concerned about the time when they go to work, and are eager to return home after work, they all rush to get on and off the boat, causing extreme crowding. In addition, the ferrymen are greedy for profit, carrying as many as 70 to 80 passengers each time. The deck and cabin are so crowded that there is no place to stand. When sailing in the river, it is extremely dangerous. In March of last year, a boat was sunk by the Customs' Jingguang Steamboat at night, resulting in the tragic drowning of more than 30 female workers. Incidents of passengers falling into the river due to crowding are also common. At around 6:00 AM yesterday, Ferry No. 4357 was loaded with more than 70 female workers from the Nanyang Tobacco Factory at the Pudong Wharf, heading towards the opposite bank. At that time, it was misty with light rain. When the ferry approached the wharf on the opposite bank, a wave suddenly rolled in, causing the boat to tilt slightly. About six or seven female workers standing at the bow of the boat fell into the river at the same time. The captain and crew of the boat, seeing the trouble they had caused, tried to rescue them. They immediately rescued four people, but two or three others were not seen resurfacing. The crew sent the rescued workers ashore, allowing them to return home on their own. After the accident, the captain and crew fled in fear of punishment. The Yangshupu Water Patrol Police learned of the incident and quickly dispatched Detective Shen Changshan and Xu Juelu to investigate. They arrested the captain Wang A'er and the crew member Sun Liujiu, and summoned Pu Fenying, a female worker from the Nanyang Tobacco Factory, as a witness. According to Wang and Sun, a small steamship passed by at the time, causing a surge of waves, which caused the boat to tilt slightly and four female workers to fall into the river. However, they had rescued them all and denied that anyone had drowned. Pu Fenying, who lives at No. 8, Lane 35, Tutitang Street, Lujiazai, Pudong, and works at the Nanyang Tobacco Factory, stated that she boarded the boat at Xiaonanyang Wharf with her sister-in-law Wang A'mao and her roommate Zuo Yuezhen at around 6:00 AM this morning to cross the river. When the boat tilted, she saw seven or eight women fall into the river at the same time. Zuo Yuezhen and her sister-in-law were among them. The crew rescued her sister-in-law and three strangers, but Zuo Yuezhen did not resurface. After being rescued, her sister-in-law drank a lot of water, had difficulty breathing, and even coughed up blood. She took her home for treatment, and her life was generally out of danger. After the police obtained the testimony, they sent a detective to summon Zuo Yuezhen's daughter Zhao Di to the police station. Zhao Di stated that her mother was 34 years old and from Siyang, Jiangbei. Her father, Zuo Yuzhang, was farming in their hometown. Only her mother, her younger sister, and herself were in Shanghai. She was 14 years old and also worked at the Nanyang Factory. She crossed the river earlier this morning and did not expect her mother to die tragically. The police head noted that the witness Pu Fenying had testified that she saw seven or eight people fall into the water, only four were rescued, and it was confirmed that one person had died. It would not be difficult to find out about the other two or three people. The defendants had violated the Customs regulations by overloading passengers and endangering public safety. He ordered them to be sent to the Local Court for questioning. Family members hired three fishing boats to search for the deceased Zuo Yuezhen all day, but had not found her by last night.

Gang Leader Bi Xiaowuzi Exposed - Forcibly Seized Embroidered Indian Silk - The Gang's Hideout and Stolen Goods Were Found

Zhao A'er, a 35-year-old native of Haimen, worked as a sailor on the Taizhou steamer. Yesterday morning, Zhao brought 25 packages of embroidered Indian silk, totaling 650 pieces, worth a considerable sum, from Haimen on behalf of a customer. He divided them into two hemp bags. After disembarking, he hired a rickshaw and placed the hemp bags on the hood and footboard of the rickshaw, intending to deliver the goods to the customer in Zhabei. However, when he arrived at the entrance of Baodai Lane in Xiaodongmen, a robber suddenly came from behind the rickshaw, first used a sharp knife to cut open the hemp bag on the hood, and then forcibly seized 50 pieces of embroidered Indian silk, carrying the stolen goods and fleeing into the small alley. Zhao, noticing the theft, quickly got off the rickshaw and shouted "Catch the thief!" However, considering the remaining goods on the rickshaw, he dared not chase after the robber and could only watch him go. He then reported the situation to the Second Precinct of the First District and requested that the police track down the robber. After receiving the report, Director Liu ordered Police Chief Li Fuyi to go to the scene and secretly investigate. They learned that the stolen goods were currently in the home of Bi Changxi, a native of Yangzhou, at No. 7 Yutang Lane in Baodai Lane. Bi, also known as Xiaowuzi, was the leader of a gang that specialized in robbing travelers' luggage near Minguo Road. The robbers under his command had to send the goods they robbed to Bi's house first, where he would divide the spoils. The robber who seized the Indian silk this time was also one of Bi's men. They immediately went to Bi's house and arrested Bi Xiaowuzi. On the spot, they found 16 pieces of the stolen Indian silk in his house. They also brought Wang Heshang, a native of Changzhou, who was also in the house, back to the precinct. After a preliminary hearing by the Director, considering that the robbery occurred in broad daylight, he ordered them to be temporarily detained for further investigation.

The Sea-Beijing Circus Opens Today

The Sea-Beijing Great Circus will open at 9:15 PM tonight at the former site of Dahua on Jing'an Temple Road and Gordon Road, with all arrangements completed yesterday. The circus will meet the eager Shanghai residents. The continuous rain has turned the entire venue into a pond, making it impossible to set foot. The circus's general manager, Mr. Sai Hui, and the owner, Mr. Hai Jingbo, spent all day personally directing workers to fill the entire venue with soil and coal slag, transforming it into a grand circus arena. On Thursday afternoon, the tall masts for the big top were erected, and the stakes were driven in. Finally, the big top was raised. At that time, there were hundreds of curious onlookers surrounding the camels, elephants, and other animals. The entire venue was surrounded by the circus's large vehicles. Some of these vehicles served as living quarters for the performers and as offices for the circus, making it extremely convenient. Yesterday afternoon, Mr. Hai Jingbo reported that regardless of the weather, the big top must be raised in time, and the first performance will proceed as scheduled tonight. The XQMA radio station will report on the interesting facts about the circus's various wild animals and their training methods. It is said that the most important secret is to use a kind attitude to win the animals' affection, and then they can be trained as desired and at will. Tigers and elephants, which seem to have deep-seated hatred and fight each other when they meet, can also be made to perform after being trained with appropriate methods. On Sunday afternoons, there will be three performances at 2:30 PM, 5:30 PM, and 9:15 PM. Next Tuesday is National Day, and to entertain the citizens, there will also be three performances at the same times as on Sunday. On other days, except for Sunday, there will be two performances each day. The circus's zoo, which has over 200 lions, tigers, and other wild animals, will be open from 10:00 AM on Sunday. Tickets are 50 cents for adults and 20 cents for children and can be purchased at the entrance to the zoo. Before each circus performance, there is usually a parade through the major streets, but due to local traffic regulations, this is not possible. To compensate, the circus will have all the animals parade around the arena in formation before each act. Once the curtain rises, there will be no intermission, ensuring that the audience leaves satisfied. On Thursday evening, Mr. Hai Jingbo rode a tiger on the back of a giant elephant, which will also be performed by the circus. Mr. Hai continued, "The polar bear may seem very gentle on the outside, but it is actually the most cunning. It lives in the Arctic and does not encounter other animals to compete with. However, once it encounters its own kind, it will fight to the death, displaying the animal's cruel and combative nature."

Further Hearing on the Extortion Case Against Lin Yaoxuan - The Court Granted the Police's Request for Another Extension

Lin Yaoxuan, a native of Sichuan, was in a clandestine meeting with Shen Wu, the wife of Shen Shou Kang, the owner of Jiankang Hospital at No. 25 Xiafei Road, in room 523 of the Central Hotel on Wuma Road at 2:00 AM on the 29th of last month. Hu Ruilin, the original matchmaker, colluded with Shen Wu's husband, Shen Shou Kang, and gathered Chen Fuliang, Li Hong, and three others to go to the hotel to extort Lin. They then kidnapped Lin to the law office of Zhang Wei at No. 105 Xuehuali Road in the French Concession and forced him to issue two promissory notes for 500 yuan each. They also seized Lin's watch and 15 yuan in cash before letting him go. Afterwards, Lin reported the incident to the French Police, who sent detectives Dai Rongji and others to arrest Hu, Chen, and Li, retrieve the watch and promissory notes, and send them to the Second Special District Court for investigation. Shen Shou Kang and his wife voluntarily surrendered to the court and were ordered to await joint trial. As reported in previous editions, yesterday morning, Judge Zhang Chaozuo continued the hearing in the Criminal Court 1. According to the police lawyer Gu Shouxi, the police investigation of the case was not yet complete, and the sixth defendant was still at large. He requested another extension for investigation and verification. However, the defendant Chen Fuliang argued loudly that the case was clear and requested that the adjournment not be granted, that the case be closed immediately, or that he be allowed to post bail. He also hired lawyers Song Yunhui and Xu Jie to defend him. As a result, the court ordered the hearing to be postponed to the 11th. The defendants were returned to custody separately. It is reported that the defendants Chen Fuliang and Shen Shou Kang have filed criminal self-prosecutions against the plaintiff, accusing him of damaging their reputations and seducing another man's wife.

A Corpse of a Worker Found on the Naocheng Wheel

While opening the hold to unload cargo on the Norwegian Qinsheng Wheel, which was docked near Yangshupu, a worker wearing blue cloth shirt and pants was suddenly found dead in the hold at 7:00 PM the night before. The sailors on the ship dragged the corpse out and reported it to the Customs Water Patrol Police, who sent Detective Xu Juelu to board the ship. It was found that the windows of the ship were closed and there were no gaps. It was presumed that the deceased did not have time to get out when the hold was closed and was suffocated to death. The corpse was sent to the Nanshi Rescue Bureau, and the Local Court was notified yesterday morning. Prosecutor Cao was appointed to conduct an autopsy and found that no family members had claimed the corpse. It was then handed over to the Bureau for burial.

Weather Report

The Xujiahui Observatory's weather forecast at 4:30 PM yesterday stated that the Yangtze River basin and coastal areas would have cloudy and foggy weather. Intermittent drizzle would continue here and in Zhejiang. Even if there were signs of clearing up, it would be very slow. There are three low-pressure centers, one in Zhejiang, one in the Yellow Sea, and one northeast of the Korean Strait, all moving slowly to the northeast. The wind force on the Shandong coast is quite strong, coming from the north to northwest. Also, in the 24 hours before 3:00 PM yesterday, the temperature in this city reached a high of 75.9 and a low of 69.3. On the same day last year, the high was 79.7 and the low was 50.7.

The National Games are Approaching - Heroes from All Directions are Entering the Capital - Teams from Sichuan, Shanxi, Anhui, Hunan, and Yunnan Arrived Yesterday - Teams from Shandong, Ping, Hubei, Liaoning, and Hong Kong are En Route

The date of the National Games is fast approaching. Athletes from various places are entering the capital one after another. The day before yesterday, there was the Gansu team, yesterday there were the Sichuan, Shanxi, Anhui, Hunan, and Yunnan teams. There were still teams expected to arrive last night. The Pinglu and Hong Kong teams are all en route. The Zhejiang Province team departs today, and this city's team is scheduled for tomorrow. The whereabouts of the athletes are recorded below.

Athletes from Sichuan, Shanxi, Hunan, and Anhui Arrive in Beijing

(Nanjing, 6th, Central News Agency) Athletes from various provinces and cities for the National Games have started their journeys to Beijing one after another. Those arriving in Beijing on the 6th included representative teams from Sichuan, Shanxi, Anhui, and Hunan provinces. The Sichuan representative team consisted of 105 people, led by chief leader Zhang Lisang. Aside from staff members, there were 74 male athletes, mostly officers and soldiers from the 20th Army. In addition to baseball and softball, they have signed up for various events. There were 14 female athletes, mostly students from Guang'an Girls' High School, participating in events such as track and field, basketball, and tennis. The Shanxi representative team consisted of 58 people, led by chief leader Wu Yunlong. Aside from staff members, there were 50 male and female athletes. The male athletes were divided into football (14), volleyball (10), basketball (9), track and field and all-around (13). The female athletes were in tennis (4). The Anhui male athlete count was 78 people, and the female athlete count was 24 people, with 17 staff members. The chief leader was Wang Shulan. In addition to putting the ball, baseball, softball, and swimming, they had joined for all other events. The Hunan representative team consisted of 127 people, led by chief leader Huang Fengqi. There were 91 male athletes, wearing blue cloth student uniforms, and 36 female athletes, wearing blue cloth shirts, short skirts, and black stockings. Their attire was simple, neat, and spirited. The male athletes had joined events such as track and field, baseball, basketball, football, and tennis. The female athletes had events such as track and field, baseball, and tennis. Other provincial and city teams such as Henan, Liaoning, Ningxia, Jilin, Heilongjiang, Harbin, and Qingdao were also expected to arrive in Beijing on the evening of the 6th. The Jiangxi team was expected to arrive on the 7th. The Guangdong team had already departed and was expected to arrive in Beijing before the 9th.

For example, the female generals from the Fourth Normal School, Yu Xiulan, Yin Sugui, and Tong Zhiying, and the female generals from Zhifu High School, Liu Ehuang, Gui, etc., are all staying in Jinan, practicing at the stadium every morning and evening. The schools in this city, such as Qilu University and the First Normal School, and the selected armed comrades are also arriving at the field on time to practice, running, jumping, or throwing weights, each doing their best. The departure date is set for 8:00 PM on the afternoon of the 5th. The athletes from outside counties only arrived in Jinan the day before yesterday. In recent days, they have been led by the instructors of each team to intensify their practice, and their progress has been remarkable. They should be able to compete with heroes from the north and south in the National Games. It is expected that the women's championship is still the most promising. All the athletes' clothing has been made, and it has been distributed in the Education Department. Jiang Shun Wheel Insults Xiang Athletes

(Nanjing, 6th) The Xiang chief leader stated that when taking the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Jiang Shun Wheel eastward this time, the comprador of the wheel and the accountant, You Xingxiang, initially agreed to a 10% discount, but then, citing that they had not received orders from the ministry to offer preferential treatment, they were extremely insulting to the male and female athletes. After much negotiation, the comprador finally accepted cash at a 60% discount. Such disobedience of orders and only knowing how to profit will definitely be reported to the Ministry of Transportation and Communications for negotiation and a request will be made to order the wheel to return the collected fare and give the comprador of the wheel appropriate punishment.

The 19th Standing Committee Meeting of the National Games Resolved - If it Rains During the Opening Ceremony, it Will be Postponed - If it Rains After the Opening, Unable to Hold the Game, It Will be Postponed in Order

(Nanjing, 6th) The 19th Standing Committee Meeting of the National Games was held at the Education Department on the evening of the 6th. All standing committee members and group leaders attended. The meeting was chaired by Chu Minyi. The main points of its resolution are as follows: (1) If it rains during the opening ceremony, it will be postponed. If it rains after the opening, unable to hold the game, it will be postponed in order. (Based on the track and field field, if the water from the stands is drained into the field after the rain, it will be too high, and the rainwater will flow into the runway. Therefore, the runway cannot be used after the rain.) (2) The meeting approved the method of the athletes' parade and oath-taking during the opening ceremony. The order of the parade will be: first, the referees, and second, the athletes, in the order of registration, with each group entering the venue. Four white lines will be used on the runway to stipulate that the runway will be circled once. Before reaching the east commander's platform, the referees will withdraw first, and one team leader will take the oath. Each unit will elect one representative and arrange themselves in an arc according to the team leader. Lift right hand and loudly swear the oath. (3) Competition and other news, each group and section should strictly keep secret and submit it to the communications section for public release. Each record should be signed by the referee group leader and then copied and distributed by the publicity section. (4) Stipulate the office of each group and section and the method of using cars. (5) The remaining examples mostly resolved, the meeting adjourned at 8:30.

### Visit Records of Athletes from Five Provinces: Sichuan, Shanxi, Anhui, Hunan, and Yunnan; Shanxi Women's Tennis Shows Promise

(Nanjing, 6th Dispatch) The Shanxi delegation of sixty-two people, led by General Team Leader Wu Yunlong and Manager Wang Songqiao, departed from Taiyuan on the 2nd of this month and arrived in Pu yesterday morning at 8:00 AM. The delegation includes eight male staff members, two female staff members, forty-seven male athletes, and five female athletes. The province brought 5,000 yuan for travel expenses for the National Games. However, because the exchange rate differs from other provinces, the entire amount was exchanged for "ring dollars" (環洋). When reporters arrived at the dormitory, everyone was organizing a large number of silver dollars in their suitcases, the clanging sound reaching outdoors. According to Mr. Wu, the province held preliminary trials in Taiyuan on the 14th of last month. Inland provinces generally do not pay much attention to sports, resulting in lagging results in various events. Among the athletes participating in this National Games, women's tennis is the most promising. The Wang Chunqing and Wang Chuncang sisters, whose mother is American and father is a returned student from America, have a completely Americanized family education. They have a strong interest in tennis. The two ladies' amazing achievements are truly a gift of their family education. In addition, there are twelve athletes from the Zhengtai Railway Guard, including one soccer player, two basketball players, and nine participating in track and field events, with Gu Desheng and Yang Hongjun's 10,000 meters being the most promising, with a time of 36 minutes and 9 seconds. ### Yunnan Team Leader Talks in Beijing

(Nanjing, 6th Dispatch) The Han delegation of one hundred and one people arrived in Beijing from Shanghai in the afternoon of the 6th, led by General Team Leader Luo Guangming, one manager, and nine athletes. According to reports, they departed from Kunming on the 21st of last month and were repeatedly subjected to unreasonable searches while passing through Annam and Hong Kong, fully experiencing the flavor of a weak nation, which was deeply distressing. Yunnan's position is similar to that of the Northeast, with the constant threat of losing the province. The enthusiastic participation of various provinces in this National Games shows the unity and struggle of the national masses, honing their skills to strengthen the physique of the masses to face the outside world. This team has been deeply touched and hopes even more for the success of the Games. School sports in Yunnan were presided over by military personnel until 1924, not knowing what ordinary sports were. After 1924, attention was gradually paid to various competitions. Currently, thanks to the advocacy of Chairman Yunlong in the province, the Provincial Sports Association has been established, with Yun serving as the chairman and Hall Director Gong Zhizhi serving as the vice chairman. Sports facilities have been slightly improved. The provincial capital has two sports fields, one sports school, and one people's education center, with small-scale basketball and volleyball courts, as well as a newly built swimming pool. Regarding the promotion of the province's sports plan, it is planned to first cultivate sports talents and gradually extend to various counties. The travel expenses for the team to Beijing are 300 yuan in national currency per person. After arriving in Beijing, the team deeply felt that the Central Sports Field is large-scale and fully equipped, and the staff of the Games are warm and helpful, for which they are immensely grateful.

The Four Knights Arrive in Hong Kong to Help Chen; South China Crushes China Four to One; South China Crushes China Four to One; The First Battle of the Open Ordinary Cup; The Two Chinese Teams Make First Contact; The Victory is Decided in the Wind and Rain

(Hong Kong Correspondence) The Hong Kong Open Ordinary Cup football match began on Saturday, with the first week of competition involving three groups in Divisions A and B. The twenty-four teams fought fiercely. However, because Division A did not have a Chinese team playing against a foreign team, it did not attract much attention from the general fans. Despite the longing for several days, few spectators attended the match that day. However, yesterday, when the two Chinese teams clashed at the Carrellin Hill Stadium, the crowd was so crowded that even though the Hong Kong Observatory hoisted Storm Signal No. 3, the enthusiasm was undiminished. Especially in the hilltop area, it was even more congested, thus affecting the match between Welsh and St. Joseph in So Kon Po. Except for some reporters, the rest were all foreigners. The details of yesterday's competition are recorded as follows:

The South China-China match was one of the most watched football matches by Chinese and Westerners. At around 4:00 PM, the two Chinese teams came out of the changing room one after another and practiced briefly in front of their respective goals. Before the players took the field, the general audience had already determined that South China was strong and unstoppable, and that China, which had been silent for a long time, had recently been thriving and should not be underestimated. No one dared to make a definitive judgment on who would win. Then, the whistle blew and the game began. The two sides clashed, and it was difficult to tell who was better. The China team was weakened because Black Head Chen Zhenhe did not come due to unforeseen circumstances, Li Hongqing's foot injury had not healed, and veterans Chen Xipei, Liang Yutang, and Lin Yuying did not appear, compared to South China, which had four knights and ten soldiers to help Chen. About fifteen minutes into the first half, Bao Jiaping scored a goal for South China. The China team did not lose heart because of the failure and tried their best to counterattack, and Lai Zhaohan returned the favor with a goal, resulting in a tie. Then, Tan Jiangbai scored again for South China, and the first half ended with a score of two to one. In the second half, the two sides changed places to fight again. The China team's defense was exhausted. Bao Jiaping took advantage of the situation and scored another goal. At the end of the game, Huang Meiyuan scored another goal. As a result, South China won by four to one. Watching this match between the two Chinese teams, there was not much brilliant performance in the game, perhaps due to the rain and slippery mud on the field. The number of free kicks awarded by the referee was also rare in ordinary matches.

The Grass Tennis Singles and Doubles Finals Are Postponed to the 21st and 22nd Due to Rain and the National Games

The Shanghai Grass Tennis Club and Senior Singles and Open Doubles Championship Finals, originally scheduled for today and tomorrow, have been postponed due to rain. Moreover, because Qiu Feihai, Wang Wenzheng, Liang Deguang, and others have to go to Nanjing to participate in the National Games, the final date has been decided to be postponed to the 21st and 22nd of this month.

The Chinese Walking Association Will Participate in the National Games Performance; Currently Negotiating the Route and Date

The Chinese Walking Association held a general membership meeting yesterday (5th) at its headquarters in Moore Hall. About fifty people attended, including Shi Jinsheng, Zhou Yuyu, Zhang Zaojiu, Zhou Ruquan, and Zhang Zhihe. The main organizer of the association, Shi Youhui, was unable to attend temporarily due to important matters, so Lu Yutian was elected as chairman and Zhang Xianlun as recorder, and the meeting was immediately convened to discuss matters such as the men's and women's open race, the international race, and participation in the National Games performance. The results were good. Finally, Shi Jinsheng and Zhou Yuyu gave speeches successively, explaining in detail the posture of walking and the points that should be paid attention to during practice. The listeners were moved. The meeting adjourned at 8:45. The decisions are as follows:

Regarding the Men's and Women's Open Race

(1) The competition date (29th of this month) is approaching, and various tasks need to be carried out urgently. In addition to Shi Youhui, Lu Yutian, and Zhang Zhaoxiang being responsible, Zhang Zhihe, Cheng Guan, Zhang Xianlun, and three others will be added to assist in everything. (2) In addition to Honorary President Cheng Yize being the ex officio chairman of the Awards Committee, Zhou Yuyu, Shi Jinsheng, Zhang Zaojiu, Ge Zhonggao, and Xu Aichen will be added as members to raise prizes. (3) It is decided to hold a full-length practice session once a week, with the association sending people to guide and hiring a horse-drawn carriage to follow in case of accidents.

Regarding the International Walking Race

(1) Since participating in the International Race, the Chinese team has won the championship for five consecutive times, which is not easy. It has added a lot of glory to the international community. Since this year's race is preparing for the 50,000-meter race at the World Games, the speed and pace may not be suitable. In addition, veterans Shi Jinsheng, Hou Genren, and others cannot practice, and their strength will inevitably be weak. They may not join the race, but those with excellent results should still join the competition. (2) After the closing of the open race, practice for the seventeen-mile race will begin immediately.

Regarding the National Games Performance

(1) This National Games will be attended by provinces and cities from almost all over the country. Take advantage of the Games to participate in the performance for publicity, in preparation for participating in the 1936 World Games in the future. The Games Organizing Committee believes that this walking event has considerable results and has approved the performance. (2) The expenses for going to Beijing to perform will be mostly settled. Shi Youhui will find a way to handle the accommodation and meals externally, and the local Bureau of Education has provided extra subsidies for travel expenses, which is greatly appreciated. (3) The performers' costumes should be Western-style dark blue tops and gray trousers, regardless of the material. When performing, they should wear blue short-sleeved T-shirts, white shorts, and white socks and black shoes to show neatness and to look good. (4) The association's emblem should be affixed to the upper left corner of the Zhuangqing top for identification. (5) Except during the performance, the performers are not allowed to wear walking shoes at ordinary times. (6) The date, route, and route of the performance will be announced after Lu Yutian is sent to Beijing in advance to negotiate. (7) The performers have been practiced once, but in order to ensure a good performance, another practice will be held at 7:00 AM this Sunday (tomorrow) morning to determine the performers.

Registration of City Examinees for the National Examination in This City Will Close on the 10th of This Month

The Central National Arts (Guoshu) Examination is approaching. The city's preparation for the city examination and selection of candidates to be sent to the examination may be insufficient. Yesterday, the Municipal Bureau of Education, the Public Security Bureau, and the Municipal National Arts (Guoshu) Museum consulted and decided to release a bulletin: The martial artists who passed the second city examination in this city should register at the Municipal First Public Sports Field on Rulin Road in the South City before the 10th of this month to be selected and sent to Beijing for the examination.

The Ministry of Education Orders Students Who Forge Certificates to Be Expelled; Those Who Forge Official Seals of Government Education Administrative Organs Will Be Sent to Court for Investigation

(Nanjing, 6th Dispatch) The Ministry of Education orders the education departments of all provinces and cities to expel students who forge certificates [blank space] from school. Those who forge official seals of government departments, [blank space], whether or not they have graduated, should be reported or sent to the competent education administrative organ for transfer to the court for investigation and prosecution according to law as soon as they are discovered.

Inauguration of the Sino-British Cultural Association Initiated by Chinese and British Figures to be Held within a Week

Cooperative movements in various fields such as knowledge, technology, and culture have been progressing rapidly since the League of Nations advocated for them. China has also been catching up quickly. Li Shizeng and others established the Chinese National Library in Geneva as the initial foundation for international cultural cooperation. Domestically, the Sino-Polish Cultural Association and the Sino-German Cultural Association have been established one after another, which has also attracted considerable attention. It is recently learned that Chinese and British figures, recognizing the long history of Sino-British relations (nearly three hundred years) and the highly developed commercial ties, believe that since the British returned the Boxer Indemnity, it is necessary to support each other in cultural and academic fields on this occasion. Although most of the refund has recently been used for construction investment, such as loans for the Yuehan Railway, the Yellow River project, and the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, which are similar to technical cooperation, the fundamental principle has been stipulated in the exchange of letters regarding the refund that the interest from this fund will be used entirely for education and cultural undertakings. This year, the Board of Trustees for the Management of the British Boxer Indemnity Fund in China has already started sending government-funded students to study in the United Kingdom, and will continue this work in the future, hoping to develop the culture of both countries. As British Minister to China, Sir Miles Lampson, is approaching his return to his country, he is eager to make a final effort in such mutually beneficial and helpful endeavors. He specially invited more than a dozen British individuals, including Meyler and, Marshall, Egland, Hughes, to initiate the Sino-British Cultural Association, which was endorsed by twenty to thirty famous figures from Chinese political and academic circles. The English prospectus has already been printed and distributed, while the Chinese prospectus is currently being translated and revised. At the same time, members are being widely recruited to enrich the internal structure. The inaugural meeting is expected to be held in the capital around the National Day. However, according to what the reporter knows, most of the initiators on the list are individuals who studied in the United Kingdom and have returned to China, such as Zhang Daofan, Chen Jian, Wang Shijie, Tao Menghe, Chen Xigeng, Hang Liwu, Li Shengwu, Qian Changzhao, Wang Xinggong, Shi Ying, Zheng Tianxi, Luo Wengan, Wu Chaochu, Song Ziliang, Ge Jingen (and Li Siguang, Ding Bianlin, Zhou Gengsheng, Chen Yuan, Xu Xinliu, Zeng Rongfu, Lu Xingyuan, Liu Haiping, Li Yingong, Ye Yaoying, etc., are all in the same category), which seems to be slightly different from other international cultural organizations. In the future, when soliciting members, this may also be used as a standard, gathering people with similar academic interests and ways of handling affairs into one group, which will be more convenient for the promotion of association affairs. After the association is established, it is heard that its main work will focus on exchanging professors, establishing libraries, exchanging publications, guiding Chinese students to study in the United Kingdom, and receiving British people to travel, study, or investigate in China, striving to achieve mutual understanding and good neighborly relations between the people of the two countries, and to benefit the cultural future of both countries.

The Vocational Guidance Research Association of Secondary Schools Holds its First Preparatory Meeting Yesterday, Passing a Draft Constitution and Research Outline, and Setting the Inaugural Meeting for the 20th of this Month

The Vocational Guidance Research Association of secondary schools in this city held its first preparatory meeting in the conference room of the Chinese Vocational Education Association at 4:00 PM yesterday.

Preparatory Meeting

The draft constitution and research outline were passed, and the inaugural meeting was scheduled for 4:00 PM on the 20th of this month in the Billeh Hall on the third floor of the Vocational Education Society. Pan Gongzhan, Chen Xuan, and He Qingxu were invited to give speeches. The details are as follows:

Preparatory Meeting: Yang Weiyu and He Qingru of the Vocational Education Society, Pan Yangyao and Yang Songgao of the Vocational Guidance Institute, Chen Jicheng of the Private Shangzhong School, Wu Zhichou of the Shanghai Girls' High School, Chen Yingmin of the Chinese Vocational School, and Xu Zhengji of the Wusong High School attended the meeting, chaired by Wu Zhichou and recorded by Yang Songgao. The chairman reported on the situation of the previous founders' meeting and then began the discussion. (1) Amended and approved the draft constitution of the association. (2) Amended and approved the research outline of the association. (3) The inaugural meeting was scheduled for 4:00 PM on the 20th of this month (Friday). (4) Mr. Jiang Wenyu was invited to be the chairman of the meeting. (5) Letters were sent to Mr. Pan Gongzhan, Mr. Chen Xuanshan, and Mr. He Qingru, inviting them to attend the meeting and give speeches. (6) The notice of the inaugural meeting should be issued in the name of the Preparatory Committee. (7) The meeting venue for the inaugural meeting was the Billeh Hall of the Vocational Education Society. (8) The order of the meeting was determined.

Research Outline

(Note) This outline is temporarily set to meet once a month and ten times a year. A total of ten research topics are proposed. The detailed items in each topic are the minimum scope to be discussed. It is best to have one person lead each discussion, make a brief introduction or report on books and newspapers related to the topic, and then have the attendees discuss it together. The content can be recorded in summary. (Topics) (1) The implementation steps of guidance in Chinese schools. How should the implementation measures outline of vocational guidance promulgated by the Ministry of Education be followed? The special circumstances of each school in Shanghai in terms of vocational guidance. How should the progress steps of each school be stipulated? What areas can be cooperated with at the beginning of implementation? (2) Personal investigation. The items that personal investigation should have. How should personal investigation be carried out? The records of personal investigation. How to use the results of personal investigation. (3) Face-to-face consultation (or personal conversation). The content of the face-to-face consultation. Who should be responsible for the face-to-face consultation? How to record the face-to-face consultation? How to encourage students to automatically request conversations? (4) Testing and reception. The function of testing in guidance. Overview of test types and content. Available tests and their uses. (5) Vocational knowledge. How to increase students' vocational knowledge. The advantages and disadvantages of vocational courses. How to train students to have the ability to collect vocational knowledge. Methods of vocational investigation. Important occupations to be investigated in this city. (6) Service ethics. Key points of service ethics. How to cultivate students' service key points. How to test students' service common sense. (7) Job placement. Placement procedures. How to contact the business community. How to organize and cooperate in the placement business. (8) Universities and secondary schools. How to investigate the real situation of universities. How to guide students to enter universities. How to seek contact between universities and secondary schools. How to promote the reform of universities. (9) Graduates. Continuing work of guidance. How to investigate the situation of graduates. How to guide graduates. How to increase the connection between students in and out of school. (10) New student guidance. Matters for new student guidance. How to carry out new student guidance. New student guidance and daily guidance.

The Second National and English Language Competition Will be Held by Universities in East China, with Nine Schools Participating, Including Shanghai University. It is Scheduled to be Held at Central University in Mid-November

The Debating Society of East China Universities, in order to enhance debating skills and interest, held the first Chinese and English speech competition in June of this year, with excellent results. The Boy Scout Review Has Been Postponed. The Defense Corps Has Been Selected to Conduct Preliminary Exercises.

Mayor Wu Tiecheng originally scheduled to review the city's Boy Scouts and the City Security Team Defense Corps on October 10 after the completion ceremony of the new City Hall building in the city center. The Boy Scouts have been rescheduled due to muddy camping conditions after the rain. The details are as follows:

Boy Scouts Rescheduled

Mayor Wu Tiecheng had ordered the City Security District Defense Corps Boy Scouts to hold a review ceremony in the city center at 10:00 AM on October 10. The City Boy Scout Council, after receiving the order, had already notified its affiliated regiments to gather in the city center at that time to await the review. However, due to muddy camping conditions after the rain, a request has been submitted to the city government to postpone the event.

Review Troops

City Defense Corps (a total of fifty-odd regiments). Because there were many troops to be reviewed on that day, the Defense Corps plans to select 648 elite members from each regiment, divided into brigades, with 208 people in each team. Each team will have a captain, three squad leaders, and a commander, who will be appointed by the Security Department.

Preliminary Exercises

A reporter from the New Voice News Agency went to the headquarters of the Defense Corps and was received by the staff. According to them, Mayor Wu Tiecheng's scope of review on Double Ten Day was too broad, so the corps decided to select a total of six elite teams, with the chief commander being appointed by the training officer of the Security Department. The six teams of this corps will be led by instructors Zhu Yuanhui and Li Ling. As for the review ceremony, it is being drafted by the Security Department. The corps has scheduled to go to the exercise at 7:00 AM on the 8th and depart at 7:00 AM on the morning of the 10th to await the review. It is also rumored that the police of the Public Security Bureau will also be reviewed on that day. According to the chief inspector of the Public Security Bureau, the Public Security Bureau has not yet received an order, and the rumor is not accurate.

The City Chamber of Commerce Boy Scout Regiment Will Hold a Full-Regiment Camp. Wang Xiaolai and Du Yuesheng Will Personally Inspect. Gather at the Regiment Headquarters at 1:00 PM Today.

The City Chamber of Commerce Boy Scout Regiment has a tradition of holding a full-regiment camp every year on the Double Ten holiday. This time, it was originally planned to participate in the city's fifth full-scale camp, but it was suddenly ordered to postpone due to rainy and slippery conditions. The regiment decided to still hold a 50-regiment camp in the city center, as various facilities have already been prepared and business holidays are exceptionally rare. All camp officials and regular members

Must gather at the regiment headquarters with personal equipment and uniforms by 1:00 PM today (reserve at 7:00 AM tomorrow), and be sent to the camp by the regiment's bus. It is also heard that the regiment affairs committee members Wang Xiaolai, Du Yuesheng, Lin Kanghou, Zheng Chengqing, etc., will all go to inspect on Double Ten Day.

Page 19

Spring and Autumn

— Yongsen

Yellow Peril

— Hutou

Speaking of the Yellow Peril, it is simply terrifying! Six hundred and fifty-seven years ago, during the reign of Emperor Ningzong of the Song Dynasty, there was a Mongol named Temujin who declared himself emperor on the Onon River, called himself Genghis Khan, destroyed the Song Dynasty, and had China, changing the country's name to Yuan and calling himself Emperor Shizu. At that time, the capital was in Yanjing, which is now Beijing. His territory stretched from the Sea of Japan in the east to Annam in the south, Siberia in the north, Asia in the west, and across Europe in the northwest. The breadth of the territory was unprecedented in Chinese dynasties. At that time, Europeans, seeing the great Chinese people of yellow race, were terrified! So they called the Chinese the Yellow Peril! Thinking back to now, being oppressed by strong neighbors everywhere, with the territory shrinking day by day and the national power weakening day by day, it is truly unbearable to look back!

Homophonous with Yellow Peril and now generally regarded as a major disaster is the [Yellow River], which is currently experiencing severe floods. According to a survey by Heping News Agency, the affected area totals 34,432 square kilometers, with as many as 27 affected areas. The people are starving everywhere, and the cries are shaking the sky. Adults and gentlemen are running around, busy with disaster relief and damming breaches. Newspapers also carry lengthy reports every day. This Yellow River flood, this Yellow Peril, is simply several times more terrible than the Yellow Peril of Genghis Khan straddling Asia and Europe!

In fact, the word [Yellow] itself is somewhat scary. A rural scholar, when deciphering this word, said, "One, two, one mu of land, planted with eight handfuls of seedlings." Just imagine, 21 mu of land, planted with only eight handfuls of seedlings, the capacity of these eight handfuls of seedlings is also quite large. Furthermore, during the Qing Dynasty, all officials such as grand ministers of the Imperial Guard and commanders of the Imperial Guard had to wear yellow jackets. When the emperor went on inspection tours, he was escorted in a carriage, with shouts and entourages in front and behind, to enhance the spectacle. In addition, civil and military ministers, either for hitting the target in the great archery competition or for meritorious service in battle, were also specially awarded yellow jackets. How majestic were these yellow jackets!

Eating

— Xing Guangyi

The most troublesome thing in running a school is not how to improve teaching methods or curriculum, but the turmoil in the dining hall, which is all about eating.

Foreigners offer wreaths to the dead, but Chinese ghosts must eat. Sometimes the rice bowl after death is more important than when alive. Therefore, there is the Confucian ethic of "There are three unfilial acts, of which having no descendants is the greatest," probably because they are afraid of not having cold pork to eat after death! Not only ghosts have to eat, but gods also have to eat. Foreigners perform rituals for gods, which can be said to be idealism. Chinese people are materialistic towards gods, which may be advocating Marxism!

Foreigners' greetings are always asking "Good morning," "Good afternoon," and "Good evening," but Chinese people's social greetings are always asking "Have you had breakfast?" "Have you had lunch?" "Have you had dinner?" It seems that Chinese people are always thinking about eating from morning till night. In fact, the rice bowl problem is indeed more important than any other problem!

Random Talk about Comics

— Qian Yun (Writing), Dong Liang (Drawing)

...Terrifying Children's Education...

Rather than saying that general writers or painters are irresponsible, it is better to frankly and clearly state that they are forced to write those irresponsible works for economic reasons, for food, with gods and monsters fully portrayed, confusing the minds of countless young Chinese citizens. After school, they eagerly go to street stalls to find those Flying Immortal Swordsmen, which cost one copper coin to rent. Each of these pamphlets often has eight to more than ten volumes. A generation of women with little knowledge also scramble to pass the time...harming them to dream of riding the clouds at night, and blowing chicken feather arrows with bamboo tubes during the day. Sure enough, children have the total sensitivity of children. Then, when a dry battery lights up, naturally...this is taken as the sword light emitted by the great hero!

Every child is like a tender seedling. To become great, it depends entirely on good education to nurture them. If children are always talking about and learning to spit flying swords, taking people's heads at will from a hundred miles away, how heartbroken should parents be that your children are so obsessed with these deeply imprinted monstrous images. To speak from a larger perspective...do you want to see all the young Chinese citizens spitting swords? If a thief has no food to eat, should we leave the back door open in advance at night?

Mystery of Romance

— Wang Ci

For several years, the call for popular literature has been very strong in the Chinese literary world. However, no matter how loud you shout, the masses are not able to reach it even with ladders. Three or four years ago, the masses were confused by the mysteries of "Proletariat" and "Bourgeoisie." A few months ago, with the arrival of George Bernard Shaw, they began to doubt the word "Humor"...Recently, there has been a popular thing called "Romance." These ingenious words make the masses feel "laughing and crying"!

In order to break the mystery of "Romance," I opened the English-Chinese dictionary and found the word Romance, which is explained as:

(1) Imaginative novel, biography, unofficial history, fictional story. (2) Events that can be regarded as novels, events of talented scholars and beautiful women, events of romance, love affairs. (3) Fiction, absurdity. (4) Delusion, infatuation, novel mind...

After reading it, I breathed a sigh of relief for the masses and couldn't help but feel something. I humbly hope that domestic literary giants who have returned from overseas will write fewer "Romances," as well as words such as "Bolshevik" and "Romantic" when writing, so that the masses can easily understand them, then the merit will be greater than reciting "Amitabha" tens of millions of times! Even if you can't help it, I hope you will write a few more "Miss," "Mister," as well as "Non-umbrella," "Friend ABC," etc., because the masses can still reach these kinds of words even with ladders!

In Orderly Fashion

— Yiguan Owner

"In orderly fashion" can also be said to be "following order." If you want to use foreign language, you can also say [In Order]. However, I am Chinese, I eat Chinese food, and this article is written in Chinese, so it is still honest to say "in orderly fashion," which is both elegant and popular, and known to women and children.

It is said, but I don't know who said it? "In orderly fashion" is what fair-haired and blue-eyed foreigners pay most attention to. Black-haired and black-eyed Chinese people are at a loss. I am just a Chinese, so at first I was furious when I heard this, feeling that it was too欺人! I thought that fair-haired and blue-eyed foreigners and black-haired and black-eyed Chinese people, although different in color, [carry their heads on their shoulders], are the same. Why do foreigners know how to pay attention to [in orderly fashion], but Chinese people don't know how to pay attention to [in orderly fashion]? Aren't these words too condescending to us Chinese?

However, thinking about it carefully, why be angry? The facts are right in front of us. Look, as soon as a ship docks, the passengers in the cabin, like a swarm of bees, all seem to be familiar with [swimming skills], not afraid of accidentally falling into the water. What women and children are the weak, everyone does not know. They only know to rush to the shore first, which is really good-looking! If a car arrives, the chaotic pushing and shoving is as lively as when the ship arrives, very interesting! As for other places, such as train stations or movie theaters, everyone is fighting for tickets, and everyone wants to be first. So, those with great strength come from behind. Those with little strength have to sigh while looking at the change. Alas! Facts like this, not knowing how to pay attention to [in orderly fashion], can indeed be seen everywhere in China, which is undeniable.

Originally, to observe whether a country's politics is on the right track and whether everything in society is sound, just look at whether its citizens are [in orderly fashion] everywhere? And you can find out. It seems that our country's politics is not on the right track, and society is a mess. Looking at the citizens everywhere who do not know how to pay attention to [in orderly fashion], maybe this is one of the many reasons?

Northeast Four Company Commanders

— Zhang Henshui

Chapter Sixteen: Sour Feelings and Breast Complaints in Front of Us Are Still Blessings; Busy Military Horses Secretly Transfer Troops

Yin Deren patted him on the shoulder and said, "Don't think so foolishly. We have to follow the orders quickly. If you sit here and worry, it's all in vain. Being a company commander is still being a company commander, and leaving is still leaving. If things are delayed and cannot be done, it will be even more terrible. Why bother?" Zhao Ziqiang thought about it and his words were correct. He had no choice but to cheer up and tell the sergeant Wang Shili to quickly make the tables and send them to the battalion headquarters that day. He still talked to Yin Deren privately, wondering how many days it would be before he left. Yin Deren said, "Don't look at them urging the tables so urgently, it's all a cover-up. With this table, the subsidy will come down from the headquarters based on this number. If the departure is delayed by one day, our boss will get a lot of benefits from it, why not delay it for a few more days? So if you have anything to do, don't worry, just take your time to do it. I don't think we'll be leaving in five days." Zhao Ziqiang put his hands in his trouser pockets and turned around in the room several times, talking to himself, "This matter is really embarrassing for me. Should I tell my old man right away? Or should I tell him when I'm about to leave?" Yin Deren smiled and said, "As the saying goes, an honest official can hardly judge family affairs, we can't give random advice on this matter. Looking at this matter, wouldn't it be better for us to be single?" Zhao Ziqiang felt even more confused after hearing his words and walked back and forth in the room non-stop. This day, he hesitated and couldn't find time to go back. Because the battalion headquarters urged the making of the tables several times in one day, there was no way but to rush to make the tables in the afternoon and send them away. The next morning, the regimental headquarters called and summoned the battalion and company commanders to a meeting. Zhao Ziqiang felt even more that the time of departure must be imminent as soon as he got this news. (208)

Children's Paradise

Fairy Tale: The Valley of the Great Serpent

— Chu Yu

At the foot of Mount Kuaiji, there was a very small lumber village. In the village lived a hunter and a woodcutter. The hunter was named Wang Si, and the woodcutter was named Zhang San. Both of these people were very lazy, but they were both getting rich, fantasizing about getting rich all day long. One day, the two of them were talking about how to get rich when an old man happened to come along. The old man heard their conversation and smiled at them, saying, "If you want to get rich, why don't you go to the mountains over there? I've heard people say that there are many gold, silver, and treasures in the valley over there. These treasures were hidden by a wealthy man who fled to the valley during the Taiping Rebellion. However, these treasures are not easy to retrieve because there is a large serpent guarding the valley entrance. In the past, people who went to search for treasure were bitten to death by the serpent, so in recent decades, no one has dared to go there again." Wang Si and Zhang San replied in unison, "That's easy. We both have knives, axes, guns, and bullets, so we're not afraid of any ferocious beasts or snakes. If this is true, we're willing to sacrifice our lives. Please, old man, tell us where the treasure is." The old man said to them, "Pass over the ridge of this mountain, then turn right, and go forward about fifty or sixty steps. There are more than twenty large pine trees. To the north of the pine forest, there is a deep valley. That valley is where the great serpent guards the treasure." Wang Si and Zhang San were overjoyed when they heard these words. They hurriedly bid farewell to the old man and rushed up the mountain. As they walked, they said, "If we get the treasure, we should divide it equally and not secretly cheat each other." The two of them swore an oath to heaven. Before long, they saw a pine forest ahead. They came to the north of the pine forest, where mist was everywhere. They searched all over the ground and, sure enough, saw a deep valley. The two were overjoyed. They each prepared their guns and knives and bravely entered the valley. After walking about twenty or thirty feet, they discovered countless gold ingots and silver bars. The two of them were ecstatic, staring at each other in a daze. Wang Si said to Zhang San, "The old man said that there was a great serpent guarding this place, but we haven't encountered anything blocking our way since we entered the valley. I really don't understand it." Zhang San said, "That old man wanted to monopolize the treasure here and deliberately deceived us." Wang Si said, "Let's quickly transport these treasures out." Zhang San, seeing so much treasure, suddenly had a wicked thought. He wanted to get all the treasure in the cave for himself, so he said to Wang Si, "Look at so much treasure. The two of us can't carry it all back. Please go home first, prepare the food, and then bring the donkey. I'll pack up the gold and silver here. When you bring the donkey, we can load it on its back together at the valley entrance." Wang Si said, "If you're here alone, what will happen if the great serpent comes out?" Zhang San said, "I have a large axe with me, so you can rest assured. Your gun and bullets are here, and you can use them to defend against the serpent if it comes." Wang Si agreed and left. When he arrived home, he had another wicked thought. He ate his own meal first, then put poison in the food that was meant for Zhang San, thinking to himself, "Zhang San, you dog thief, your fate is in my hands now." He hurriedly led the donkey up the mountain. At this time, Zhang San was waiting for Wang Si under the pine forest. Seeing Wang Si walking halfway up the mountain, he quickly aimed and fired the gun. With a bang, Wang Si died from the bullet. Zhang San saw that Wang Si was dead, so he walked to Wang Si's side, led the donkey to the valley entrance, and sat alone on a stone, laughing loudly, "All these treasures are mine now, and I'll enjoy them for the rest of my life." As he spoke, he unwrapped the food from the donkey's back and devoured it ravenously. Just as he was about to get up to transport the gold and silver, he suddenly experienced severe abdominal pain, was poisoned, fell to the ground, and died. This cycle of retribution all stemmed from insatiable greed and mutual jealousy. Harming others harms oneself. It is truly a satisfying story.

Financial: American Silver, Prices Fall; Gold Market Stable, Up Slightly by Two Cents; Foreign Telegrams Initially Grim, Then Favorable; Market Fluctuates and Rebounds

The gold market remained stable yesterday, with a relatively calm outlook. The morning began with the overseas silver market showing an increase in London and a decrease in the U.S., with fluctuating exchange rates. The forward silver price at the Metal Exchange decreased by between 1.5 and 3 cents. London spot gold decreased by 3.5 pence. The price of new U.S. mined gold was $31.50, slightly down by 2.4 cents from the previous day. Stocks fell by 5.5 cents, U.S. cotton decreased by 20 points, and U.S. wheat decreased by 1.5 cents. The market opened lower due to a Reuters telegram reporting that President Roosevelt would return from New York to Washington today, with new developments in the recovery situation, but then fell. However, the situation stabilized slightly after Senator Robinson, a Democrat, declared that inflation would hinder the recovery movement, and that the dollar price should be reset and prices strictly adjusted. The opening situation was flat, with HSBC postings unchanged, resulting in no upward or downward movement. Subsequently, due to strong bank appetite, the Bank of East Asia and the Bank of Communications bought up U.S. dollars. Foreign telegrams stated that the U.S. indicated a fixed gold standard at the war debt conference, driving prices up to over $80. The market then fell again, and the market was quiet, with Guangdong banks supplying the market. Raw gold was priced at $1,120. The Double Tenth Gold Exchange will also be closed for one day. Today's market conditions will be recorded later.
